ذلكَ ، ولو أرادَ اللهُ تعالى بهم خيراً لما عَصَوا .
ونحو هذا : ما أنكرَهُ المعتزلة مِنْ جوازِ العَفْوِ عَمَّنْ ماتَ مُصِرّاً على المعاصي ، وإنكار الشفاعة له ، وإنكار خلْقِ الجنَّةِ والنار ، ومثل هذا كثير في العقائدِ
ويدلُّ قطعاً على هذا التأويل الذي ذكرناه : إتيان عمر بنِ عبدِ العزيز بمثل هذا جواباً للسائل عن الأهواء ، فكأنَّهُ قالَ لَهُ : عليكَ الدين بما كانَ عليه السلفُ ، وتلقَّاهُ منهم الخلفُ ، ودع ما يناقضُ ذلك ممَّا أحدثه المبتدعة
بل نقولُ : هذهِ الألفاظ التي اغترَّ بها مَنْ مَالَ إِلى التقليدِ ، وحَذَرَ مِنَ النظرِ في التوحيدِ .. هي في الحقيقةِ حُجَّةٌ عليهِ لا له ؛ لأنَّ علماء السنَّةِ رضوانُ اللهِ عليهم إنَّما ألَّفوا في علم التوحيد ليبينوا للناس ما كانَ عليه السلف الصالح ، وصارَ لشهرته ووضوحه قبل ظهورِ البدع ديناً لعجائزهم وإمائِهم وأهْلِ بذوهم وصبيانِ كُتَّابِهم ، وزادوا بأنْ حصنوه بالبراهين العقليّةِ التي تنتهي إلى ضرورات العقل ، بحيثُ يخرجُ مَنْ أنكرها عن ديوان العقلاء ، وبالأدلَّةِ النقليَّةِ القطعية فيما تقبلُ فيهِ ، فهم رضي الله عنهم جعلوا على حرزِ دين الإسلام أسواراً لما قدمَتْ جيوشُ المبتدعة التي لا تُحصى كثرة تريد استلابَ ذلك الدين وإبداله بجهالات يهلِكُ مَن اتَّبَعَها .
ثم لمَّا أَتَتِ المبتدعةُ بمعاولِ الشبهات لتهدم بها أسوار الأدلَّةِ ، وبسلالم الأوهام والتخيُّلاتِ لتتجاوز بها إلى حرز الدين.. بالغَتِ العلماءُ رضي الله عنهم في الاحتياط للدين ، ونظرَتْ بعين الرحمة لجميع المسلمينَ ، فأفسدَتْ عليهم تلك الشبهات ، وفسخَتْ لهم تلك الأوهام والتخيُّلاتِ ؛ بأجوبة قاطعة لا يجد العاقل عن الإذعانِ إليها سبيلاً ، وأنفقوا رضيَ الله عنهم في جميعِ ذلك الذخائر التي حصلت لهم مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ وأصحاب رسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، الذينَ هُمُ القدوة لهذه الأمَّةِ ، وقد كان حرزُ الدين محفوظاً في عهدِ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أنْ يتجاسر أحدٌ يرومُ الاختلاس منه ، وإنَّما تجاسرَ مَنْ تجاسر عندَ غَيبتِهِ ، لكن لم يمت صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ حتى وَرَّثَ علماءَ أُمَّتِهِ وأهلَ سُنَّتِهِ مِنَ المعارفِ ما يدفعونَ بِهِ كلَّ عدو يريدُ الاختلاس مِنْ دينهم أَحَلَّ أُمَّتَهُ فِي حِرْزِ مِلَّتِهِ كَاللَّيْثِ حَلَّ مَعَ الْأَشْبَالِ فِي أَجَمٍ
فحين قدم الأعداء بعد موتِ النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لهدم حصنِ الدين .. أنفقوا في تحصينه أعظم تحصين تلك الذخائر التي ورثوها واستعملوا آلاتِ عقولهم في وجوه إنفاقها ، ولم تزل أرباح تلكَ الذخائرِ مِنْ زيادةِ المعارفِ تتوالى عليهم ، وينفقونها عند الاحتياج إليها ، فهذا حال علماء السنَّةِ الذين تكلموا في علم التوحيدِ ، وألفوا فيه التواليف ، جزاهُمُ اللهُ أفضل جزاء .
فبالله أيُّها المقلّد الذي يستدل بما لا يحيطُ بِهِ علماً ؛ مَنْ كانَ يقفُ لرد أهل البدع حين خاضوا معَ كثرتهم وعظيم احتيالهم في شبهاتِهم
That, and if Allah Most High had willed good for them, they would not have disobeyed. And similar to this: what the Mu'tazila denied of the permissibility of pardoning those who die persisting in sins, and their denial of intercession for him, and their denial of the creation of Paradise and Hell, and much like this in the creeds. And it indicates decisively upon this interpretation which we have mentioned: the coming of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz with such a response to the questioner about the desires, as if he said to him: 'Upon you is the religion as it was upon the predecessors, and the successors received it from them, and leave what contradicts that of what the innovators have introduced.' Rather we say: these expressions by which he was deceived who inclined to blind following, and feared from rational reflection in tawḥīd, are in reality a proof against him, not for him; because the scholars of the Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them, only authored works on the science of tawḥīd to clarify for the people what the righteous predecessors were upon, and due to its fame and clarity before the appearance of innovations, it became the religion of their elderly women, their female servants, the people of their households, and the children of their schools. And they further fortified it with rational proofs that lead to necessities of the intellect, such that whoever denies them leaves the register of the rational people, and with definitive transmitted proofs in what admits them. They, may Allah be pleased with them, placed walls around the fortress of the religion of Islam, when the armies of the innovators advanced—countless in number—seeking to plunder that religion and replace it with ignorances by which whoever follows them perishes. Then when the innovators came with pickaxes of doubts to demolish the walls of the proofs, and with ladders of fantasies and illusions to transcend to the fortress of religion, the scholars, may Allah be pleased with them, were extreme in precaution for the religion, and looked with an eye of mercy upon all Muslims. They invalidated those doubts for them, and dismantled those fantasies and illusions with decisive answers to which a rational person finds no way but submission. And they spent, may Allah be pleased with them, in all that, the treasures that had accrued to them from the Book, the Sunnah, and the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, who are the role models for this community. And the fortress of the religion was protected during the time of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, from anyone daring to attempt to steal from it. But those who dared, dared only during his absence. However, he did not die, peace and blessings be upon him, until he bequeathed to the scholars of his community and the people of his Sunnah from the knowledges that with which they repel every enemy who wishes to steal from their religion. 'He placed his community in the protection of his religion like a lion settled with his cubs in a thicket.' For even when the enemies came after the death of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, to demolish the fortress of the religion, they spent in fortifying it the greatest fortification from those treasures which they inherited, and they employed the instruments of their intellects in the ways of spending them. And the profits of those treasures—from increase of knowledges—kept coming to them, and they spend them when needed. Such is the state of the scholars of the Sunnah who spoke about the science of tawḥīd and authored works about it. May Allah reward them with the best reward. So by Allah, O blind follower who uses as evidence that which he does not fully know: who would stand to repel the people of innovation when they engaged with their great number and great cunning in their doubts?
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the science of kalām (speculative theology) against those who condemn it as an innovation. The author (likely Sanusi or a commentator) presents a refutation of the position of the 'muqallidūn' (blind followers) who rely on transmitted expressions forbidding theological reasoning. The argument proceeds in several steps: First, the author gives examples of heretical positions (e.g., Mu'tazilite denial of pardon for grave sinners, intercession, and creation of Paradise and Hell) to show the danger of abandoning reasoned theology. Second, he cites the Caliph 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Azīz, who told a questioner to adhere to the religion of the salaf and reject innovations, implying that the anti-kalām stance contradicts the salaf's practice. Third, the author makes his central claim: the very phrases used by those who fear speculative theology are actually a proof against them, because the scholars of the Sunnah wrote works on tawḥīd to clarify the creed of the salaf. Far from being a novelty, the creed was so clear that even common people followed it, but the scholars later fortified it with rational proofs (barāhīn 'aqliyya) to defend against the innovators. These proofs lead to intellectual necessities, and rejecting them excludes one from the community of rational people. The author employs the metaphor of a fortress: the scholars built walls (of proofs) around the religion when the armies of innovators attacked. When the innovators used pickaxes of doubts and ladders of fantasies, the scholars responded with decisive arguments, using the treasures inherited from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and Companions. The author then quotes a line from al-Būṣīrī's Burda comparing the Prophet placing his community in the protection of his religion to a lion in a thicket. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: after the Prophet's death, the scholars spent these treasures to strengthen the religion, and the blind follower should ask himself who would stand against the innovators with their great numbers and cunning if he rejects the tools of kalām? Thus, the passage argues that the science of tawḥīd, including rational proofs, is not an innovation but a necessary defense of orthodoxy.

Key Terms
المبتدعة (al-mubtadiʿa)
الشفاعة (al-shafāʿa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Salaf never engaged in any theological argumentation and simply accepted doctrines without question.
Correction: This passage shows that the Salaf, represented by Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, actively identified and rejected innovations, implying they did engage in distinguishing truth from falsehood, which requires rational discernment.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi cite as an example of Mu'tazilite denial?
A) Denial of the existence of angels
B) Denial of intercession for grave sinners
C) Denial of the necessity of prayer

Key Takeaway
The Salaf did not remain silent when core doctrines were denied; they actively rejected innovations, which implies that some form of theological reasoning is necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a group denying intercession or the existence of Paradise and Hell, does your heart respond with the same concern that Sanusi and the Salaf had? If not, what is holding you back from actively defending these core beliefs?
?
The Salaf's method was not silence but clear rejection of innovation. Think of a subtle doubt or deviation you've encountered in your own circle. Have you ever chosen silence over reasoned correction because it felt safer? How can you change that starting today?
?
You now see that the Salaf themselves used theological reasoning to defend the creed. Is there any part of your aqeedah that you are neglecting to think through rationally out of fear of being like the Mu'tazila? What step will you take this week to strengthen your understanding of that doctrine?

The Scholars' Use of Rational Proofs
Sanusi argues that rational proofs are a fortress for the creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's central claim that the scholars of the Sunnah authored works on tawḥīd and fortified the creed with rational proofs, contrary to the claim that kalām is an innovation.

Core Idea
Rational proofs are the fortress walls protecting the creed of the Salaf.

Having shown the danger of abandoning theology, Sanusi now makes his core argument. He turns the tables on those who oppose kalām by claiming that the very texts they use to forbid it are actually evidence against them. The scholars of the Sunnah did not shy away from rational reflection; rather, they authored comprehensive works on tawḥīd, clarifying the creed of the Salaf and then fortifying it with rational proofs that lead to intellectual necessities.

Guided Path
1
Read the central claim carefully
Sanusi says the expressions used by the 'muqallidūn' (blind followers) are a proof against them. Identify what those expressions are and why they backfire.
The key is that the scholars' works themselves demonstrate the use of reason.
2
Understand the relationship between the Salaf's creed and rational proofs
Sanusi explains that the creed of the Salaf was initially clear and well-known, so even common people followed it. But when innovations appeared, the scholars fortified it with rational proofs (al-barāhīn al-ʿaqliyya). Note that these proofs are not a departure from the Salaf's way but a defense of it.
Rational proofs are presented as a shield, not a new doctrine.
3
Reflect on the consequences of denying these proofs
Sanusi states that whoever denies these rational proofs 'leaves the register of the rational people.' This is a strong rhetorical move—it equates rejection of kalām with irrationality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلكَ ، ولو أرادَ اللهُ تعالى بهم خيراً لما عَصَوا .
ونحو هذا : ما أنكرَهُ المعتزلة مِنْ جوازِ العَفْوِ عَمَّنْ ماتَ مُصِرّاً على المعاصي ، وإنكار الشفاعة له ، وإنكار خلْقِ الجنَّةِ والنار ، ومثل هذا كثير في العقائدِ
ويدلُّ قطعاً على هذا التأويل الذي ذكرناه : إتيان عمر بنِ عبدِ العزيز بمثل هذا جواباً للسائل عن الأهواء ، فكأنَّهُ قالَ لَهُ : عليكَ الدين بما كانَ عليه السلفُ ، وتلقَّاهُ منهم الخلفُ ، ودع ما يناقضُ ذلك ممَّا أحدثه المبتدعة
بل نقولُ : هذهِ الألفاظ التي اغترَّ بها مَنْ مَالَ إِلى التقليدِ ، وحَذَرَ مِنَ النظرِ في التوحيدِ .. هي في الحقيقةِ حُجَّةٌ عليهِ لا له ؛ لأنَّ علماء السنَّةِ رضوانُ اللهِ عليهم إنَّما ألَّفوا في علم التوحيد ليبينوا للناس ما كانَ عليه السلف الصالح ، وصارَ لشهرته ووضوحه قبل ظهورِ البدع ديناً لعجائزهم وإمائِهم وأهْلِ بذوهم وصبيانِ كُتَّابِهم ، وزادوا بأنْ حصنوه بالبراهين العقليّةِ التي تنتهي إلى ضرورات العقل ، بحيثُ يخرجُ مَنْ أنكرها عن ديوان العقلاء ، وبالأدلَّةِ النقليَّةِ القطعية فيما تقبلُ فيهِ ، فهم رضي الله عنهم جعلوا على حرزِ دين الإسلام أسواراً لما قدمَتْ جيوشُ المبتدعة التي لا تُحصى كثرة تريد استلابَ ذلك الدين وإبداله بجهالات يهلِكُ مَن اتَّبَعَها .
ثم لمَّا أَتَتِ المبتدعةُ بمعاولِ الشبهات لتهدم بها أسوار الأدلَّةِ ، وبسلالم الأوهام والتخيُّلاتِ لتتجاوز بها إلى حرز الدين.. بالغَتِ العلماءُ رضي الله عنهم في الاحتياط للدين ، ونظرَتْ بعين الرحمة لجميع المسلمينَ ، فأفسدَتْ عليهم تلك الشبهات ، وفسخَتْ لهم تلك الأوهام والتخيُّلاتِ ؛ بأجوبة قاطعة لا يجد العاقل عن الإذعانِ إليها سبيلاً ، وأنفقوا رضيَ الله عنهم في جميعِ ذلك الذخائر التي حصلت لهم مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ وأصحاب رسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، الذينَ هُمُ القدوة لهذه الأمَّةِ ، وقد كان حرزُ الدين محفوظاً في عهدِ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أنْ يتجاسر أحدٌ يرومُ الاختلاس منه ، وإنَّما تجاسرَ مَنْ تجاسر عندَ غَيبتِهِ ، لكن لم يمت صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ حتى وَرَّثَ علماءَ أُمَّتِهِ وأهلَ سُنَّتِهِ مِنَ المعارفِ ما يدفعونَ بِهِ كلَّ عدو يريدُ الاختلاس مِنْ دينهم أَحَلَّ أُمَّتَهُ فِي حِرْزِ مِلَّتِهِ كَاللَّيْثِ حَلَّ مَعَ الْأَشْبَالِ فِي أَجَمٍ
فحين قدم الأعداء بعد موتِ النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لهدم حصنِ الدين .. أنفقوا في تحصينه أعظم تحصين تلك الذخائر التي ورثوها واستعملوا آلاتِ عقولهم في وجوه إنفاقها ، ولم تزل أرباح تلكَ الذخائرِ مِنْ زيادةِ المعارفِ تتوالى عليهم ، وينفقونها عند الاحتياج إليها ، فهذا حال علماء السنَّةِ الذين تكلموا في علم التوحيدِ ، وألفوا فيه التواليف ، جزاهُمُ اللهُ أفضل جزاء .
فبالله أيُّها المقلّد الذي يستدل بما لا يحيطُ بِهِ علماً ؛ مَنْ كانَ يقفُ لرد أهل البدع حين خاضوا معَ كثرتهم وعظيم احتيالهم في شبهاتِهم
That, and if Allah Most High had willed good for them, they would not have disobeyed. And similar to this: what the Mu'tazila denied of the permissibility of pardoning those who die persisting in sins, and their denial of intercession for him, and their denial of the creation of Paradise and Hell, and much like this in the creeds. And it indicates decisively upon this interpretation which we have mentioned: the coming of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz with such a response to the questioner about the desires, as if he said to him: 'Upon you is the religion as it was upon the predecessors, and the successors received it from them, and leave what contradicts that of what the innovators have introduced.' Rather we say: these expressions by which he was deceived who inclined to blind following, and feared from rational reflection in tawḥīd, are in reality a proof against him, not for him; because the scholars of the Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them, only authored works on the science of tawḥīd to clarify for the people what the righteous predecessors were upon, and due to its fame and clarity before the appearance of innovations, it became the religion of their elderly women, their female servants, the people of their households, and the children of their schools. And they further fortified it with rational proofs that lead to necessities of the intellect, such that whoever denies them leaves the register of the rational people, and with definitive transmitted proofs in what admits them. They, may Allah be pleased with them, placed walls around the fortress of the religion of Islam, when the armies of the innovators advanced—countless in number—seeking to plunder that religion and replace it with ignorances by which whoever follows them perishes. Then when the innovators came with pickaxes of doubts to demolish the walls of the proofs, and with ladders of fantasies and illusions to transcend to the fortress of religion, the scholars, may Allah be pleased with them, were extreme in precaution for the religion, and looked with an eye of mercy upon all Muslims. They invalidated those doubts for them, and dismantled those fantasies and illusions with decisive answers to which a rational person finds no way but submission. And they spent, may Allah be pleased with them, in all that, the treasures that had accrued to them from the Book, the Sunnah, and the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, who are the role models for this community. And the fortress of the religion was protected during the time of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, from anyone daring to attempt to steal from it. But those who dared, dared only during his absence. However, he did not die, peace and blessings be upon him, until he bequeathed to the scholars of his community and the people of his Sunnah from the knowledges that with which they repel every enemy who wishes to steal from their religion. 'He placed his community in the protection of his religion like a lion settled with his cubs in a thicket.' For even when the enemies came after the death of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, to demolish the fortress of the religion, they spent in fortifying it the greatest fortification from those treasures which they inherited, and they employed the instruments of their intellects in the ways of spending them. And the profits of those treasures—from increase of knowledges—kept coming to them, and they spend them when needed. Such is the state of the scholars of the Sunnah who spoke about the science of tawḥīd and authored works about it. May Allah reward them with the best reward. So by Allah, O blind follower who uses as evidence that which he does not fully know: who would stand to repel the people of innovation when they engaged with their great number and great cunning in their doubts?
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the science of kalām (speculative theology) against those who condemn it as an innovation. The author (likely Sanusi or a commentator) presents a refutation of the position of the 'muqallidūn' (blind followers) who rely on transmitted expressions forbidding theological reasoning. The argument proceeds in several steps: First, the author gives examples of heretical positions (e.g., Mu'tazilite denial of pardon for grave sinners, intercession, and creation of Paradise and Hell) to show the danger of abandoning reasoned theology. Second, he cites the Caliph 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Azīz, who told a questioner to adhere to the religion of the salaf and reject innovations, implying that the anti-kalām stance contradicts the salaf's practice. Third, the author makes his central claim: the very phrases used by those who fear speculative theology are actually a proof against them, because the scholars of the Sunnah wrote works on tawḥīd to clarify the creed of the salaf. Far from being a novelty, the creed was so clear that even common people followed it, but the scholars later fortified it with rational proofs (barāhīn 'aqliyya) to defend against the innovators. These proofs lead to intellectual necessities, and rejecting them excludes one from the community of rational people. The author employs the metaphor of a fortress: the scholars built walls (of proofs) around the religion when the armies of innovators attacked. When the innovators used pickaxes of doubts and ladders of fantasies, the scholars responded with decisive arguments, using the treasures inherited from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and Companions. The author then quotes a line from al-Būṣīrī's Burda comparing the Prophet placing his community in the protection of his religion to a lion in a thicket. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: after the Prophet's death, the scholars spent these treasures to strengthen the religion, and the blind follower should ask himself who would stand against the innovators with their great numbers and cunning if he rejects the tools of kalām? Thus, the passage argues that the science of tawḥīd, including rational proofs, is not an innovation but a necessary defense of orthodoxy.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlīd)
البراهين العقلية (al-barāhīn al-ʿaqliyya)
علم التوحيد (ʿilm al-tawḥīd)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what did the scholars of the Sunnah do to protect the creed from innovations?
A) They forbade all discussion of theology
B) They fortified it with rational proofs
C) They ignored the innovators
D) They changed the creed to accommodate innovations

Key Takeaway
The scholars' use of rational proofs is not a departure from the Salaf's way but a necessary defense of their clear creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on inherited beliefs without personal reflection, or do you actively seek to understand and defend your tawḥīd with your intellect? What would it mean for you to 'fortify' your faith as the scholars did?
?
Have you ever seriously examined the rational foundations of your belief in Allah? If not, what is holding you back from doing so, and are you willing to take that step today?
?
If you are responsible for teaching others about Islam, are you equipping them with both the simple creed and the intellectual tools to defend it against doubts? Or are you leaving them vulnerable to confusion?

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
The Fortress Metaphor and Defense of the Religion
Sanusi describes the scholars as defenders of the religion's fortress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the fortress metaphor to describe the scholars' role as defenders of Islam, and why he concludes that blind followers are helpless against innovators.

Core Idea
The scholars are the lion-like guardians of the religion's fortress.

In the final part of his defense, Sanusi employs a powerful metaphor: the religion is a fortress, and the scholars have built walls of proofs around it. When the armies of innovators attack with doubts and fantasies, the scholars use the intellectual treasures inherited from the Prophet and the Salaf to repel them. The passage culminates in a rhetorical challenge to the blind follower, asking who would stand against the innovators if not for the scholars of kalām.

Guided Path
1
Understand the fortress metaphor
Sanusi describes the religion as a 'fortress' (ḥirz) and the scholars as builders of walls (aswār). Identify what these walls represent—the rational and transmitted proofs.
The fortress protects against plunder by innovators.
2
Follow the narrative of attack and defense
The innovators come with pickaxes (maʿāwil) of doubts and ladders (salālim) of fantasies. The scholars respond with decisive answers (ajwiba qāṭiʿa). Notice the imagery of war.
This emphasizes the seriousness of the threat.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical conclusion
Sanusi ends with a direct address to the 'blind follower' (al-muqallid), asking who would repel the innovators if not for the scholars. This drives home the necessity of kalām.
The question is meant to provoke self-criticism.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the science of kalām (speculative theology) against those who condemn it as an innovation. The author (likely Sanusi or a commentator) presents a refutation of the position of the 'muqallidūn' (blind followers) who rely on transmitted expressions forbidding theological reasoning. The argument proceeds in several steps: First, the author gives examples of heretical positions (e.g., Mu'tazilite denial of pardon for grave sinners, intercession, and creation of Paradise and Hell) to show the danger of abandoning reasoned theology. Second, he cites the Caliph 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Azīz, who told a questioner to adhere to the religion of the salaf and reject innovations, implying that the anti-kalām stance contradicts the salaf's practice. Third, the author makes his central claim: the very phrases used by those who fear speculative theology are actually a proof against them, because the scholars of the Sunnah wrote works on tawḥīd to clarify the creed of the salaf. Far from being a novelty, the creed was so clear that even common people followed it, but the scholars later fortified it with rational proofs (barāhīn 'aqliyya) to defend against the innovators. These proofs lead to intellectual necessities, and rejecting them excludes one from the community of rational people. The author employs the metaphor of a fortress: the scholars built walls (of proofs) around the religion when the armies of innovators attacked. When the innovators used pickaxes of doubts and ladders of fantasies, the scholars responded with decisive arguments, using the treasures inherited from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and Companions. The author then quotes a line from al-Būṣīrī's Burda comparing the Prophet placing his community in the protection of his religion to a lion in a thicket. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: after the Prophet's death, the scholars spent these treasures to strengthen the religion, and the blind follower should ask himself who would stand against the innovators with their great numbers and cunning if he rejects the tools of kalām? Thus, the passage argues that the science of tawḥīd, including rational proofs, is not an innovation but a necessary defense of orthodoxy.

Checkpoint
What do the scholars use to invalidate the doubts of the innovators?
A) Force and intimidation
B) Decisive answers and proofs
C) Ignoring them
D) Changing the religion

Key Takeaway
The scholars of kalām are the necessary defenders of the faith, using intellectual weapons to protect the fortress of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi warns against being a 'blind follower' (المقلد) who does not truly know their evidence. In what areas of your faith are you merely following without understanding? Name one belief you hold that you could not defend with solid proof from the Qur'an and Sunnah. What will you do this week to change that?
?
The scholars looked with 'an eye of mercy upon all Muslims' when they refuted innovators. Think of a person you know who holds a mistaken view about Islam. Do you feel mercy or frustration towards them? Write down one practical step you can take to correct them with mercy, as the scholars did.
?
The Prophet bequeathed knowledge to the scholars to protect the religion after him. Are you actively inheriting that knowledge, or are you neglecting it? If you were to die today, what legacy of defending the truth would you leave behind? Commit to one action today that strengthens your role as a defender of your faith.

Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
The Fortress of the Salaf
Explains the security of the salaf and the command for the weak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early salaf were immune to innovation and why weak-minded persons are commanded to enter their secure fortress.

Core Idea
The salaf's fortress is secure because they mixed only with truth, not with innovators.

Sanusi begins by explaining that the righteous predecessors (salaf) enjoyed a unique immunity to innovation. Their strong command of Arabic, deep understanding of Quran and Sunnah, and avoidance of mixing with people of innovation made their creed the safest. For this reason, a person of weak insight is instructed not to wander into debate but to take shelter in the fortress of their belief, defended by capable imams.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the salaf's immunity
Notice the two reasons given: the people of innovation do not seek to mix with them, and the salaf's own linguistic and intellectual purity.
The word 'حرز' (fortress) is key.
2
Understand the command for the weak
The author commands the weak of insight to belong to this fortress, citing again the lack of mixing and the presence of defending imams.
3
Reflect on the imams' role
Consider the hardships the imams endured to protect the fortress. This shows that the fortress is not passive but actively defended.
The imams are described as expansive in views and powerful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مأمون ، وأهل البدع لا يقصدونهم بالمخالطة ، فأمنوا مِنَ التلوث بأقذار البدع على عقائدِهم التي أتقنوها ؛ بما يُحتاج إليهِ مِنَ البراهين ، على حسَبِ ما أخذوهُ مِنَ السلف الصالح ، وفهموهُ مِنَ الكتابِ والسنَّة ؛ لسهولة ذلكَ عليهم ؛ إذ هم عرب لم تستول على ألسنتهم العُجمةُ ، ولا صَعِدَ على قلوبهم رانُ الجمودِ ولا ظُلمة الغباوة ، فعقائدهم أسلم شيءٍ وأحسنُهُ ، فلهذا أُمِرَ ضعيفُ النظرِ أنْ ينتمي إلى حرز دينهم المأمونِ ؛ لعدم المخالطة لأهل البدع ، ولوقوفِ أئمةِ زمانهم المتّسعينَ في الأنظارِ ، ولهمُ القُوَّةُ العظمى في الذهنِ واللسانِ رضيَ الله عنهم .. أمامَ حرزِ دينهم (۱) ، يدفعون عنهم كل مبتدع وضال ، وتحمّلوا في ذلك رضي الله عنهم مِنْ مَشاق النظر والإذاية في الأنفس والمالِ ما يُعظَمُ اللهُ بِهِ أَجورهم . [1 إحالة ضعيف النظرِ على السلف إحالة على جهالة ] ولو قيل لضعيف النظرِ الذي حيَّرَتْهُ الأهواء : عليك بما عليه الصحابة.. لكانَ إحالة على جهالةٍ ؛ إذْ كُلٌّ مِنْ أَهْلِ البدع يَدَّعِي أَنَّ ما ينتحله هو مذهب الصحابة ، فكانَ مِنَ الحزمِ والصوابِ ما أَمرَ بهِ علماء السلفِ مِنَ الانتماء إلى الحرز المأمونِ الذي وقفَتْ أبطال العلماء لمناضلة أعداء الدين أمامَهُ ، والضعيفُ إذا لم يدخل الحرزَ ووقف موقف الأبطالِ . . خيف عليهِ أَنْ يُهْلِكَهُ العدو لضعفِهِ . ولهذا أيضاً مالَ الفخرُ في موطن الموت لحرز الضعفاء ودعا به ؛ لأنه موطن يَتشَتَّتُ فيهِ الفكرُ لعظيم هولِهِ ، فيُخشى إِنْ أَقبلَتْ فيهِ وارداتُ الشُّبَهِ أَنْ يَضعُفَ العقلُ عن دفعها ، وأقل ما فيها تكدر العقل بظلمتها ، والزمانُ والفكرُ ضاقا في ذلك الموطن الهائل عن حمل ذلك ، فدعا بصفاء المعرفة والحفظ ممَّا يُكدِّرُها ، كما هو شأن عجائز تلك الأزمنة وضَعَفَتِهم ؛ أنَّهم عرفوا العقائد بما لا بدَّ منهُ مِنْ أَدلَّتِها. ولم يبحثوا عن الزائد ، ولا انتصبوا لمناظرة أهل البدع ، فصفَتْ عقائدهم حتى ماتوا على ذلكَ ، هذا مراده والله أعلم .
Secure, and the people of innovation do not intend to mix with them, so they are safe from contamination with the filth of innovation upon their creeds which they perfected; with what is needed of proofs, according to what they took from the righteous predecessors (salaf) and understood from the Book and the Sunnah; because that was easy for them; since they were Arabs, non-Arabic speech did not dominate their tongues, nor did the rust of stagnation or the darkness of dullness ascend upon their hearts, so their creeds are the safest thing and the best. Therefore, the weak of insight was commanded to belong to the secure fortress of their religion; due to lack of mixing with the people of innovation, and because the imams of their time, who are expansive in views and possess great power in mind and tongue, stand before the fortress of their religion, repelling from them every innovator and misleader, and they endured in that, may Allah be pleased with them, from the hardships of investigation and harm to themselves and wealth, that Allah magnifies their rewards. [1 Referring the weak of insight to the predecessors is a referral to ignorance] And if it were said to the weak of insight, whom the passions have confounded: 'You must follow what the Companions were upon,' that would be a referral to ignorance; since every one of the people of innovation claims that what he adopts is the school of the Companions. So it was from prudence and correctness what the scholars of the salaf commanded: belonging to the secure fortress, before which the champions of scholars stood to fight the enemies of religion. And if the weak one does not enter the fortress and stands in the position of the champions, it is feared that the enemy might destroy him due to his weakness. For this also, al-Fakhr inclined at the moment of death to the fortress of the weak and prayed with it; because it is a place where thought scatters due to the greatness of its terror, so it is feared that if the incursions of doubts come upon it, the intellect may weaken in repelling them, and the least of what is in it is the clouding of the intellect by their darkness. And time and thought are too constrained in that tremendous moment to bear that, so he prayed for purity of knowledge and preservation from what clouds it, just as is the case of the old women of those times and their weak ones: that they knew the creeds with what is necessary of their proofs, and did not investigate the extra, nor did they set themselves up to debate the people of innovation, so their creeds were pure until they died upon that. This is his meaning, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage explains why the early salaf (righteous predecessors) were safe from innovation and why weak-minded persons are commanded to adhere to their 'secure fortress'. The author begins by stating that the people of innovation do not seek to mix with the salaf, so the salaf were safe from contamination. Their creeds were perfected with the necessary proofs derived from the Quran and Sunnah, and this was easy for them because they were pure Arabs, free from non-Arabic influence, stagnation, and dullness. Hence their creeds are the safest and best. Therefore, a person of weak insight is commanded to belong to their secure fortress for two reasons: (1) lack of mixing with innovators, and (2) because the great imams of the time stand before that fortress defending against innovators, enduring hardships. The author then addresses an objection: why not simply tell the weak person to follow the Companions? He explains this would be a referral to ignorance, because every innovator claims to follow the Companions. So the proper command is to enter the fortress guarded by the champions of scholars. If the weak person stands outside among the champions, he may be destroyed. The author then mentions that Imam al-Razi (al-Fakhr) at the moment of death prayed for the fortress of the weak, because death is a terrifying moment where doubts may assail the intellect; thus he prayed for purity of knowledge and preservation, like the old women who knew just enough proofs to have sound creeds without engaging in debate. This, the author says, was his intended meaning.

Key Terms
حرز الدين
السلف الصالح
ضعيف النظر
أهل البدع
المخالطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The salaf simply followed tradition without rational proofs.
Correction: The passage states they perfected their creed with the necessary proofs from the Book and Sunnah, and it was easy for them due to their linguistic purity.

Checkpoint
Why were the salaf safe from contamination by innovators?
A) They never met innovators.
B) Innovators did not seek to mix with them, and they had pure tongues and minds.
C) They were too strong to be influenced.
D) They only associated with the same school.

Key Takeaway
The salaf's creed is safe because they mixed only with truth, and the weak should take shelter in it under the protection of capable scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever allowed yourself to mix frequently with people who openly oppose core Islamic beliefs, thinking you are strong enough to resist? Based on this passage, what is the safer path, and are you willing to take it even if it costs you relationships?
?
The imams endured hardships in body and wealth to defend the fortress. What hardship have you endured recently to protect your creed from innovation? If none, what is one concrete step you can take this week to strengthen your fortress?
?
You are commanded to belong to the secure fortress of the salaf. Do you actively seek the protection of scholars who are expansive in views and strong in evidence, or do you rely on your own limited understanding? Could your reluctance to submit to sound scholarship be a form of arrogance that exposes you to the filth of innovation?

Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
The Correct Guidance for the Weak-Minded
Answers the objection about referring to the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why referring the weak-minded simply to 'follow the Companions' is insufficient, and how the fortress analogy resolves this.

Core Idea
Pointing to the Companions is vague because every innovator claims them; the fortress specifies the guarded truth.

After establishing the security of the salaf's fortress, Sanusi anticipates an objection: why not just tell the weak person to follow the Companions? He explains that this would be a referral to ignorance, because every innovator claims to follow the Companions. Instead, the correct guidance is to enter the fortress defended by the scholars. He illustrates this with the example of Imam al-Razi at death and the simple faith of old women.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Notice the hypothetical question and Sanusi's critique: referring to the Companions is ambiguous because innovators also claim them.
2
Understand the fortress analogy
The fortress is not just any group; it is the one guarded by the champion scholars who fought heretics. The weak must enter it, not stand outside among the champions.
3
Reflect on the example of al-Razi and the old women
Even the great scholar al-Razi at death sought the fortress of the weak, and the old women maintained pure creed by knowing only necessary proofs without debating.
This shows the wisdom of not overburdening the weak with excessive debate.

Source Text

Misconception: Following the salaf is just blind imitation (taqlid).

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi reject the simple instruction 'follow the Companions' for the weak person?
A) Because the Companions had differing views.
B) Because every sect claims to follow the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek guidance about your faith, do you look for clear, specific markers or do you rest on general statements like 'follow the righteous predecessors'? Sanusi warns that such vagueness leaves you prey to every innovator. Today, will you examine whether you are hiding in a secure fortress or just hoping a label will save you?
?
Al-Razi, a great scholar, turned to the fortress of the weak at death. Your intellect will scatter in that moment. If your creed is not pure and simple — free from extra details and debates — what will happen when doubts flood in? Have you truly anchored your heart to the necessary proofs, or have you entertained curiosities that cloud faith?
?
The old women knew just enough to die with pure creeds. Are you content with that kind of knowledge, or does your pride demand you debate and investigate beyond necessity? Be honest: is your pursuit of 'more knowledge' actually protecting you or distracting you from the fortress?

Method of Learning
intermediate

Refutation of Interpreting al-Razi's Prayer as Blind Taqlid
Refutes the claim that al-Razi's prayer endorses blind taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Razi's prayer for the faith of the weak cannot be interpreted as advocating blind taqlid, and what it actually means.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's prayer was for purity of faith, not for ignorance.

In this passage, the author counters a misinterpretation of a famous prayer by Imam al-Razi. Some claimed he was seeking blind imitation (taqlid), but the author shows this is impossible — it would mean praying for ignorance. Instead, the prayer is about protection from doubts, reflecting al-Razi's own intellectual struggles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the strong language used to reject the blind taqlid interpretation.
2
Understand the first argument
The author argues that interpreting the prayer as seeking blind taqlid would mean praying for removal of knowledge, which is irrational and displeasing to any intelligent person.
3
Examine the concession
Even if we assume al-Razi meant old women who blindly imitate, the prayer must be interpreted as seeking the consequence of their belief: absence of doubts, combined with al-Razi's own knowledge.
This shows the author is being thorough in refuting the claim.
4
Consider the possible cause
The author speculates that al-Razi's deep engagement with philosophers' arguments and his difficulty in answering them may have led him to pray for simple faith.
This is a charitable explanation that avoids accusing al-Razi of advocating ignorance.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Think about how this passage protects against misinterpreting scholarly prayers and emphasizes the importance of knowledge in faith.
The key is that the prayer is for purity, not for ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا حمله على طلب الاعتقادِ التقليدي (۱) : فهو دعاء بسلب المعرفةِ والعياذُ باللهِ ، والانتقال إلى ما هو أدنى ، وفي إيمان صاحبِهِ مِنَ الخلافِ ما عُلِمَ ، والدعاء بمثلِهِ لا يرضاه عاقل ، ولو سلمنا أَنَّهُ أراد العجائز المقلداتِ.. لوجبَ أَنْ يُحمَلَ دعاؤُهُ على لازم اعتقادِهنَّ ؛ وهو عدم خطورِ الشبهاتِ بالبالِ مضموماً إلى كمال معرفتِهِ هو ؛ لتكونَ إِذْ ذاك صافية عن كلِّ مُكدِّرٍ . وقد يحتمل أنْ يكونَ سببُ دعائِهِ بهاذا ما عُلِمَ مِنْ حالِهِ مِنَ الولوعِ بحفظ آراء الفلاسفة وأصحاب الأهواء ، وتكثيرِ الشُّبَه لهم وتقوية إيرادِها ، معَ ضعفِهِ عن تحقيقِ الجواب عن كثير منها على ما يظهرُ مِنْ تواليفِهِ ، ولقدِ استَرَقُوهُ في بعض العقائدِ (۲) ، فخرج إلى قريبٍ مِنْ
As for interpreting it as seeking blind taqlid, it is a prayer for the removal of knowledge, and we seek refuge with Allah from that, and a transition to what is lower, and in the faith of its possessor there is known disagreement, and no rational person would be pleased with such a prayer. And even if we concede that he intended the old women who are blind imitators, it would be necessary to interpret his prayer as referring to the necessary consequence of their belief: which is the absence of doubts occurring to the mind, combined with his own perfection of knowledge, so that it would then be pure from every contaminator. And it is possible that the cause of his prayer with this is what is known of his state: his obsession with preserving the opinions of the philosophers and people of desires, and multiplying doubts for them and strengthening their presentation, while being weak in achieving the answer to many of them, as appears from his writings, and indeed they stole him in some creeds, so he came out close to
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Imam al-Razi's prayer (mentioned in the previous lesson) was a call to blind taqlid (uncritical imitation). The author argues strongly: interpreting it as seeking blind taqlid would mean praying for the removal of knowledge, which is in reality a prayer for ignorance—something no intelligent person would request. Furthermore, faith based on blind imitation is a matter of scholarly disagreement regarding its validity. Even if we assume al-Razi meant the old women who merely imitate, we must interpret his prayer as seeking the necessary consequence of their belief: namely, that no doubts enter their minds, combined with his own complete knowledge—so that his knowledge remains pure and untroubled. The author then suggests another possible reason for al-Razi's prayer: al-Razi was known for his deep engagement with the arguments of philosophers and heretics, presenting and strengthening their doubts, yet he was sometimes unable to answer them adequately. As a result, the philosophers and heretics 'stole' him in some doctrines, meaning they influenced him, and he came close to adopting their views. Thus, his prayer for the faith of the weak was perhaps a plea to be protected from such influence.

Key Terms
الاعتقاد التقليدي
التقليد
العجائز المقلدات
الشبهات
الفخر الرازي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that al-Razi's prayer for the faith of the weak is an endorsement of blind taqlid.
Correction: The author shows that such an interpretation would mean praying for ignorance, which is irrational. Instead, the prayer is about preservation from doubts and a reflection of al-Razi's own struggles.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against interpreting al-Razi's prayer as seeking blind taqlid?
A) Because blind taqlid is forbidden in the Quran.
B) Because such an interpretation would mean praying for removal of knowledge, which is irrational.
C) Because al-Razi himself was a blind imitator.
D) Because the old women do not practice taqlid.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's prayer is a plea for preservation from doubts, not an endorsement of blind imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself praying for a simple faith while your mind is entangled with doubts? What practical step can you take today to purify your intention while continuing to seek knowledge?
?
The author suggests that philosophers 'stole' al-Razi in some beliefs. Is there any idea, relationship, or pursuit that has 'stolen' your heart from complete reliance on Allah? What would it cost you to let it go?
?
If you were in al-Razi's position, would you pray for protection from doubts or for more intellectual strength? Why does your answer reveal about where you place your trust?

Critique of al-Razi's method and the danger of doubts
Critique of al-Razi's method and defense of simple faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the controversy surrounding al-Razi's prayer for the faith of old women and why excessive engagement with philosophical doubts is warned against.

Core Idea
Engaging with doubts without ability to refute can corrupt faith.

In this passage, the author critiques the method of Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, who was known for extensively studying philosophical doubts. The author interprets al-Razi's own prayer for a simple faith and warns that his approach led him close to heresy. This lesson explores the fine line between defending faith and being overwhelmed by doubts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Note that the passage contains a poem at the end.
2
Identify the two interpretations of al-Razi's prayer
The passage presents two possible interpretations of al-Razi's prayer: one as a desire for pure faith like old women, and another as a call to blind imitation (taqlid). Pay attention to how the author rejects the latter.
The author favors the first interpretation and argues it is not taqlid.
3
Understand the critique of al-Razi's methodology
The passage criticizes al-Razi for his obsession with philosophical doubts and his inability to refute them properly. This led scholars to warn against his works.
Look for the quote from al-Maqqari and the poem by Ibn Taymiyya.
4
Reflect on the warning from scholars and the poem
Consider why studying excessive doubts without strong refutation is dangerous. The poem calls al-Razi's work 'knowledge without religion' and 'inspiration of the devils.'
This reinforces the lesson's core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنه موطن يتشتت فيه الفكر لعظيم هوله، فيخشى إن أقبلت فيه واردات الشبه أن يضعف العقل عن دفعها، وأقل ما فيها تكدر العقل بظلمتها، والزمان والفكر ضاقا في ذلك الموطن الهائل عن حمل ذلك، فدعا بصفاء المعرفة والحفظ مما يكدّرها، كما هو شأن عجائز تلك الأزمنة وضعفتهم؛ أنهم عرفوا العقائد بما لا بد منه من أدلتها. ولم يبحثوا عن الزائد، ولا انتصبوا لمناظرة أهل البدع، فصفت عقائدهم حتى ماتوا على ذلك، هذا مراده والله أعلم.
وأما حمله على طلب الاعتقاد التقليدي: فهو دعاء بسلب المعرفة والعياذ بالله، والانتقال إلى ما هو أدنى، وفي إيمان صاحبه من الخلاف ما علم، والدعاء بمثله لا يرضاه عاقل، ولو سلمنا أنه أراد العجائز المقلدات.. لوجب أن يحمل دعاؤه على لازم اعتقادهن؛ وهو عدم خطور الشبهات بالبال مضموماً إلى كمال معرفته هو؛ لتكون إذ ذاك صافية عن كل مكدّر.
وقد يحتمل أن يكون سبب دعائه بهذا ما علم من حاله من الولوع بحفظ آراء الفلاسفة وأصحاب الأهواء، وتكثير الشبه لهم وتقوية إيرادها، مع ضعفه عن تحقيق الجواب عن كثير منها على ما يظهر من تواليفه، ولقد استرقوه في بعض العقائد، فخرج إلى قريب من شنيع أهوائهم، ولهذا يحذر الشيوخ من النظر في كثير من تواليفه. قال الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن محمد بن أحمد المَقَرِّي التِّلِمْسَانِي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه: (من تحقق كلام ابن الخطيب وجده في تقرير الشبه أشد منه في الانفصال عنها، وفي هذا ما لا يخفى) أنشدني شيخي أبو عبد الله الآبلي، قال: أنشدني عبد الله بن إبراهيم الزموري، قال: أنشدني تقي الدين بن تيمية لنفسه:
[من البسيط]
محصل في أصول الدين حاصله
من بعد "تحصيله" علم بلا دين
أصل الضلالة في الإفك المبين
فما فيه فأكثره وحي الشياطين
Because it is a place where thought becomes scattered due to the enormity of its terror. So it is feared that if incoming doubts advance therein, the intellect might weaken in repelling them. The least of what they contain is the clouding of the intellect by their darkness. Time and thought are constrained in that immense place from bearing that. So he prayed for purity of knowledge and preservation from that which would cloud it, as was the case of the old women of those times and their weak ones: they knew the beliefs by what is necessary of their proofs. They did not seek beyond that, nor did they set themselves up to debate the people of innovation. So their beliefs became pure until they died upon that. This is his intent, and Allah knows best.
As for interpreting it as seeking traditional blind imitation, then it is a prayer for the removal of knowledge – Allah forbid – and transitioning to what is lower. In the faith of its possessor there is disagreement as is known. No rational person would be pleased with such a prayer. Even if we grant that he intended the imitating old women, then his prayer must be interpreted as referring to the necessary consequence of their belief – which is the non-occurrence of doubts in the mind, coupled with his own complete knowledge – so that it would then be pure from every clouding.
It is also possible that the reason for this prayer of his is what is known of his state: his obsession with preserving the opinions of the philosophers and the people of whims, multiplying doubts for them and strengthening their presentation, along with his inability to achieve a satisfactory answer to many of them, as appears from his works. They (the philosophers) even stole from him in some beliefs, and he came close to their vile whims. For this reason, the shaykhs warn against studying many of his works. Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Maqqari al-Tilimsani, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said: 'Whoever examines the words of Ibn al-Khatib will find him more severe in presenting doubts than in disconnecting from them, and in this there is no concealment.' My shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Abuli narrated to me, saying: Abdullah ibn Ibrahim al-Zammuri narrated to me, saying: Taqi al-Din ibn Taymiyya recited to me from his own composition:
[al-Basit]
The 'Muhassal' in the principles of religion – its sum
After its 'Tahsil' is knowledge without religion.
It is the root of misguidance in manifest slander.
Most of what is in it is inspiration of the devils.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage offers a critique of the methodology of Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (referred to as Ibn al-Khatib). It begins by describing a fearful situation – probably the state of facing doubts in matters of faith – where the mind can become scattered and weakened by the darkness of such doubts. The author then interprets a prayer attributed to al-Razi (a prayer for the state of old women) as a desire for a faith that is pure and simple, like that of old women who only know essential proofs and do not engage with extra arguments or debates with innovators. This is presented as the proper, safe method.

The passage then sharply rejects the interpretation that al-Razi's prayer was a call to blind imitation (taqlid). It argues that such an interpretation would be a prayer for the removal of knowledge, which no rational person would endorse. Even if the prayer referred to imitating old women, it must be understood as a desire for a faith free from the intrusion of doubts, combined with the perfect knowledge of the one praying (i.e., al-Razi himself).

The author then goes further to suggest a possible reason for al-Razi's prayer: his known inclination to study the views of philosophers and people of whims, and his excessive presentation of their doubts while being unable to provide adequate refutations. As a result, he was influenced by them in some beliefs and came close to their heretical positions. Therefore, the scholars warn against studying many of his works.

To support this criticism, a statement from al-Maqqari is quoted, noting that al-Razi is more effective at presenting doubts than at refuting them. Finally, a poem by Ibn Taymiyya is cited, attacking al-Razi's famous work 'Muhassal' as producing 'knowledge without religion' and being largely 'inspiration of the devils.' The overall lesson is a strong warning against the method of engaging excessively with philosophical doubts without the ability to refute them, advocating instead for the safer approach of the early Muslims.

فلسفة (falsafah)
ابن الخطيب (Ibn al-Khaṭīb)
تحصيل (taḥṣīl)
ابن تيمية (Ibn Taymiyya)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Razi's prayer for the faith of old women was a call to blind imitation (taqlid).
Correction: The passage argues it was a prayer for a faith free from doubts while retaining necessary knowledge, not for abandoning knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the shaykhs warn against studying many of al-Razi's works?
A) Because his works contain heretical beliefs that he himself adopted.
B) Because he was more skilled at presenting doubts than at refuting them, and he was influenced by philosophers.
C) Because his works are too difficult for the average student.
D) Because he openly rejected the authority of the early scholars.

Key Takeaway
Excessive engagement with philosophical doubts without the ability to refute them can lead to corruption of faith, as seen in the case of al-Razi.

?

Refutation of the Companion-Ignorance Objection
The author refutes the claim that the Companions' ignorance of kalam terms justifies taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Companions' ignorance of later kalam terminology does not invalidate rational inquiry or justify blind imitation (taqlid).

Core Idea
Knowledge of terms is not knowledge of proofs; the Companions knew the proofs deeply.

Some object that the greatest Companions like Abu Bakr and 'Umar died without knowing terms like jawhar (substance) and 'arad (accident), so why should we engage in kalam? Sanusi refutes this by distinguishing between technical labels and the actual rational proofs from the Qur'an. He shows that the Companions had profound understanding of the faith, far beyond mere terminology, and that their example does not support taqlid.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening sentence that states the objection: the Companions died without knowing jawhar and 'arad. This is used to argue that kalam is unnecessary.
Notice the objector relies on an argument from silence.
2
Read Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi expresses amazement that anyone would cite this as evidence. He asks: what connection do conventional terms have with the actual proofs of beliefs? Ignorance of terms does not imply ignorance of proofs.
Focus on the rhetorical question that exposes the logical gap.
3
Analyze the analogy
Sanusi compares the objection to someone claiming Companions were ignorant of Arabic grammar or rhetoric because they didn't use later technical terms. This analogy shows the absurdity.
The analogy highlights that technical terminology is a later development, not essential to understanding.
4
Examine the condition for validity
Sanusi says the objection would only be valid if the Companions died knowing God by mere taqlid, ignoring nazar (rational consideration) and misunderstanding the Qur'anic proofs. He asserts this is false.
The author makes a conditional statement that reinforces the necessity of nazar.
5
Appreciate the praise of Companions
Sanusi concludes by praising the Companions' intelligence and knowledge, stating that even a lowly female slave among them had more religious knowledge than the greatest scholars of his time.
This elevates the Companions' understanding beyond mere terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ـ وهو قوله : مات أبو بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما ولم يعرفا الجوهر والعَرَضَ ، وكذلك سائر الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم - : فأنا أعجبُ أنْ يَذكُرَ مثلَ هذا دليلاً على التقليدِ مَنْ لَهُ أدنى تمييز ، فأَيُّ للألفاظ المصطلح عليها في شيءٍ مِنْ أَدلَّةِ العقائدِ حتى يلزمَ مِنَ الجهل بشيء منها الجهلُ بشيءٍ مِنَ الأدلَّةِ ؟! وما أشبه هذا بقولِ مَنْ يقولُ : إِنَّ الصحابة رضوانُ اللهِ عليهم كانَتْ تجهل المقصودَ مِنْ علم العربيةِ ؛ لأنَّهم ماتوا ولم يعرفوا حقيقةً الفاعل ولا المفعول ولا الحالِ والتمييز المصطلح عليها عند علماء العربية ، أو كانوا يجهلونَ المقصودَ مِنَ البلاغة ؛ لأنَّهم كانوا يجهلونَ ألفاظاً فيها أحدثها مَنْ بعدهم اصطلاحاً ! وهل هذه الأقوال تصدرُ مِنْ عاقل أُلهِم رشدَهُ ؟! وإِنَّما يصح لهُ الاستدلال لو ثبتَ لهُ أنَّ الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم ماتوا ولم يعرفوا اللهَ إلا بمُجرَّدِ التقليدِ ، وأعرضوا عن النظرِ الذي حثَّ تعالى عليه في آي مِنْ كتابِهِ ، وأنَّ أدلَّةَ العقائدِ التي لا تُحصى كثرةً في القرآنِ كانَتْ تمرُّ عليهم ولم يفهموا وجه دلالتِها ، وصحة هذا عنهم مما يأباه كلُّ مؤمن . [ حدَّةُ ذكاء الصحابة الكرامِ رضيَ الله عنهم ووفور علمهم ] وما أحوج مَنْ يُعرِّضُ بمثل هذهِ النقيصة في علي مناصبهم التي لا تُلحَقُ .. لعظيم الأدب ! ولقد نقطعُ أنَّ أكابر علماء زماننا لم يحصل لهم مِنَ العلم بالدين وسننه ما حصل لأدنى أَمَةٍ مِنْ إماء الصحابة
As for the first — which is his statement: 'Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may God be pleased with them, died without knowing jawhar (substance) and 'arad (accident), and likewise the rest of the Companions, may God be pleased with them' — I am amazed that someone with the least discrimination would mention such as evidence for taqlid (imitation). For what connection do the conventional terms have with anything from the proofs of the beliefs such that ignorance of something of them entails ignorance of something of the proofs?! And how similar this is to the statement of one who says: 'The Companions, may God be pleased with them, were ignorant of the objective of the science of Arabic; because they died without knowing the reality of al-fa'il (subject), al-maf'ul (object), al-hal (circumstantial adverb), and al-tamyiz (specification) as conventionally understood by the scholars of Arabic; or they were ignorant of the objective of balaghah (rhetoric); because they were ignorant of terms in it that were invented as conventions by those after them!' And do such statements emanate from a rational person inspired with rectitude?! His inference would only be valid if it were established for him that the Companions, may God be pleased with them, died without knowing God except by mere taqlid, and turned away from the consideration (nazar) that the Exalted has urged in verses of His Book, and that the proofs of the beliefs, which are countless in the Qur'an, used to pass over them without their understanding the aspect of their indication; and the correctness of this about them is rejected by every believer. [The sharpness of the intelligence of the noble Companions, may God be pleased with them, and the abundance of their knowledge] And how much more in need of sublime respect is the one who exposes such a deficiency in their lofty positions that cannot be attained! And we certainly conclude that the greatest scholars of our time have not obtained from knowledge of the religion and its sunnah what was obtained by the lowest female slave among the female slaves of the Companions.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims: Abu Bakr and 'Umar died without knowing the terms 'jawhar' (substance) and 'arad' (accident), and all Companions likewise; therefore, kalam is unnecessary and taqlid suffices. The author refutes this by pointing out that technical terms have no necessary connection to the actual proofs of beliefs. Ignorance of labels does not imply ignorance of the proofs themselves. He draws an analogy: if someone argued that the Companions were ignorant of Arabic grammar and rhetoric because they didn't know later technical terms, that argument would be absurd. The objector's inference would only hold if the Companions died knowing God by mere blind imitation, ignoring the rational consideration (nazar) that God explicitly commands and the countless proofs in the Qur'an that they would have failed to understand. This is rejected by every believer. The author then adds a subtitle praising the sharp intelligence and vast knowledge of the Companions, noting that even a lowly female slave among them possessed more religious knowledge than the greatest scholars of the author's time. This reinforces that the Companions had deep understanding, just not the later terminological framework.

Key Terms
جوهر
عَرَض
تقليد
نظر
دلائل العقائد
صحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the Companions did not use kalam terminology, then they must have practiced taqlid and so can we.
Correction: Sanusi shows that technical terms are not the same as the proofs themselves; the Companions understood the proofs and engaged in nazar, so their example does not support taqlid.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against using the Companions' ignorance of 'jawhar' and 'arad' to justify taqlid?
A) The Companions actually knew these terms
B) Technical terms are not identical to the proofs of beliefs
C) The Qur'an does not contain rational proofs
D) Taqlid is obligatory for everyone

Key Takeaway
The Companions' lack of later kalam terminology does not imply they lacked understanding; they possessed deep knowledge of the proofs from the Qur'an and engaged in rational consideration (nazar).

?
When you hear a sophisticated theological term like 'jawhar' or 'arad', do you feel intimidated or dismissive? What does that reaction reveal about your trust in your own intellect versus the tradition?
?
The author says the Companions had knowledge far beyond our greatest scholars. If you honestly evaluate your own understanding of the Qur'an's proofs, how much closer are you to the Companions' level than you think? What concrete step will you take this week to move closer?

Later Terminologies and Ibn Furak's Statement
Author explains purpose of later terminologies and interprets Ibn Furak's saying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose of later kalam terminologies and the correct interpretation of Ibn Furak's statement regarding substance and accident, and why it does not support blind following (taqlid).

Core Idea
Later kalam terms are tools, not requirements for salvation.

This passage addresses a common misconception: that technical kalam terms are necessary for true knowledge of Allah. The author clarifies that these terms were introduced only to ease learning, and that salvation depends on knowing Allah without taqlid, not on familiarity with philosophical vocabulary. He then interprets Ibn Furak's famous saying to reinforce this point and defends the Companions from the charge of being blind followers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Notice the author's flow: purpose of terms → Ibn Furak's saying → clarification → defense of Companions.
Pay attention to the key terms: اصطلاحات, تقليد, جوهر, عرض.
2
Identify the two key claims
First, the author states that later terminologies are only for convenience, not essential. Second, he explains that Ibn Furak's statement does not validate taqlid. Locate these claims in the Arabic text.
The phrase 'لأن معرفة الحق موقوفة عليها' is negated.
3
Reflect on the defense of the Companions
The author argues that the Companions' lack of exposure to later terms does not imply they were muqallid. Consider why accusing them of taqlid would be a grave slander.
The word 'المقلدين' (blind followers) is contrasted with the Companions' direct knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنّما أحدثَ المتأخّرونَ مِنَ الاصطلاحاتِ ما أحدثوا ؛ لتَخِفَّ المؤنة عليهم في التعلم والتعليم ، لا لأن معرفة الحق موقوفةٌ عليها . وإلى هذا المعنى أشار أبو بكر بنُ فُورَكَ بقولِهِ : ( لو لم يدخل الجنةَ إِلا مَنْ عرفَ الجوهر والعرض .. لبقيَتْ خاليةً )، ونحنُ نقولُ بموجبه، ونقولُ معَ ذلكَ : لا يدخلُ الجنةَ إِلا مَنْ هو عارف بالله تعالى ولم يُقلّد في ذلك، عرف الجوهر والعرض أو لم يعرفهما، فليس في قولِ ابنِ فُورَكَ ما يدلُّ على صحةِ التقليدِ، ولا في عدم اطلاع الصحابة على اصطلاحات أحدثَها المتأخّرونَ ما يدلُّ على أَنَّهم كانوا مُقلِّدِينَ ومَنْ ظَنَّ بالصحابة رضي الله عنهم أنَّهم كانوا في إيمانِهم فقد أعظم عليهمُ الفِرية ، وجهل قدرَهمُ الأعظم .
And indeed, the later ones only introduced what they introduced of terminologies to lighten the burden upon themselves in learning and teaching, not because knowledge of the truth depends upon them. Abu Bakr ibn Furak indicated this meaning by his statement: 'If only those who knew the substance and accident were to enter Paradise, it would remain empty.' And we affirm its import, and we say along with that: Only one who knows Allah Almighty and does not blindly follow in that enters Paradise, whether he knew the substance and accident or did not know them. So, in the statement of Ibn Furak there is nothing that indicates the validity of blind following (taqlid), and nor does the fact that the Companions were unaware of terminologies introduced by later ones indicate that they were blind followers. And whoever thinks that the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, were blind followers in their faith has indeed greatly slandered them and is ignorant of their immense status.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a defense of later kalam terminologies and a clarification of Ibn Furak's famous statement. The author begins by stating that later scholars introduced terminological distinctions only to ease learning and teaching, not because knowledge of divine truth is contingent on them. He then cites Ibn Furak's remark: if Paradise were only for those who know substance and accident, it would be empty. The author affirms this but adds a crucial clarification: the condition for entering Paradise is knowledge of Allah without taqlid, regardless of familiarity with philosophical terms. Therefore, Ibn Furak's statement does not support taqlid; it merely emphasizes that technical knowledge is not mandatory. Similarly, the Companions' lack of exposure to later terminologies does not imply they were muqallid. To accuse them of taqlid would be a grave injustice.

ابن فورك
تقليد
جوهر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Furak's statement implies that technical kalam terms (like substance and accident) are necessary for salvation, or that lacking them justifies blind following (taqlid).
Correction: The author explicitly states that Ibn Furak's words do not indicate the validity of taqlid, and that salvation depends on knowledge of Allah without blind imitation, not on knowing technical terms.

Key Takeaway
Later kalam terminologies are helpful tools, not essential for salvation; what matters is knowing Allah without blind imitation.

6 min
Proof that the Sahaba Were Not Muqallid
Sanusi argues that the Companions were not muqallid by citing the Prophet's clear proofs and long teaching period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Companions' faith was based on clear evidence and not blind following.

Core Idea
The Companions were guided by clear proofs, not blind custom.

Sanusi presents a powerful historical argument to show that the Companions were not mere followers of tradition. He contrasts the stubbornness of non-Arab pagans with the zeal of the Arabs, then recounts how Bedouins demanded a clear sign from the Prophet and received it. The Prophet's thirteen years of teaching before warfare further establish that his followers embraced Islam based on evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the flow of the argument from non-Arabs to Arabs to the specific incident.
The passage is a single continuous argument, not a list.
2
Identify the comparison with non-Arabs
The author begins by noting that even non-Arab pagans defended their ancestral religion fiercely, only abandoning it after clear truth appeared. This sets the stage for the Arabs.
3
Note the Bedouin incident
A group of Bedouins demanded a sign (aya) from the Prophet, and he provided one. They understood Arabic well and grasped the proof. This shows they required evidence.
4
Consider the thirteen years of teaching
The Prophet taught for thirteen years without warfare, clarifying proofs until only the obstinate remained. Even a short period of such teaching removes taqlid from a learner.
5
Draw the conclusion about the Companions
If even simple learners are freed from taqlid by the Prophet's teaching, how much more the Companions who learned directly from him? Thus, they were not muqallid.
This is the main point the author is proving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد كانَ سائرُ الكَفَرَةِ مِنَ الأَعاجِمِ يَذْبُونَ عن دينهم ودينِ آبائهم بالسيف وبغيره، ويرضَوْنَ بالموتِ وبسبي النساء والذريَّةِ دونَهُ، فما رجعوا إلا بعد ظهورِ الحقِّ وقيامِ عَلَمِ الصدقِ، فكيف بالعربِ المعروفين بأعظم حمية لدينهم ؟! ولقد دعا النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ جماعةً مِنْ حواشي الأعراب، فطالبوه بالآية الدالة على صدقِهِ، فأظهر لهم ما قامَتْ الحُجَّةُ به، ولقد كانوا يفهمونَ الكلام العربي فهماً وافياً بالمعاني، حاوياً لمقاصدِ الخطابِ، والقرآنُ العظيم مملوء بالحُجَج والبراهين التي لا تُحصى كثرةً، وقد أقامَ بينهمُ المُعلَّمُ الأكبر المبعوث لسياسة الخلق، أفصحُ الخَلْقِ، والمُعْطَى جوامع الكلام والشفقة التامة على عبادِ اللهِ، صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .. ثلاث عشرة سنةً مِنْ غيرِ قتال يُوضّحُ الأدلَّةَ، ويقيمُ الحُجَّةَ، إلى أن ظهر الحق ظهوراً لم يبقَ معَهُ إِلا المعاندة معَ كمال المعرفةِ، وبالنزر اليسيرِ مِنْ هذهِ المدَّةِ يحصل بتعليم الألكن وذي العِيِّ وقصور العقل مِنَ المعلمين للأبله والبليد مِنَ المتعلمينَ ما يخرجُ بهِ عنِ التقليدِ في عقائدِهِ خروجاً تاماً، فكيف ترى حالَ مَنْ تلقَّى العلم مباشرةً ممَّنْ عمَّ نورُهُ البسيطة كلَّها، بل مَنْ نوره أصلُ الأنوارِ كلَّها، ومَنِ العقولُ كلُّها بالنسبة إلى عقلِهِ كَمَنْ أَخذَ حصاةً
And indeed, all the disbelievers among the non-Arabs used to defend their religion and the religion of their fathers with the sword and otherwise, and they accepted death and the capture of women and children rather than [abandon] it. They only turned back after the appearance of the truth and the establishment of the banner of sincerity. So how [would it be] with the Arabs, known for their greatest zeal for their religion?! The Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, once called a group from the outskirts of the Bedouins, and they demanded a sign indicating his truthfulness, so he showed them what established the proof for them. And they used to understand Arabic speech with a complete understanding of meanings, encompassing the purposes of discourse. And the Mighty Qur'an is filled with proofs and evidences that are countless. And the greatest teacher, sent to manage creation, the most eloquent of creation, granted the comprehensive speech and perfect compassion for the servants of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, spent thirteen years without warfare, clarifying the proofs and establishing the evidence, until the truth appeared in a manner that left nothing but obstinacy along with complete knowledge. And by the smallest amount of this period, through the teaching of the stammerer, the tongue-tied, and the limited intellect from the teachers to the simpleton and the dull among the learners, there is achieved what completely removes him from blind following (taqlid) in his beliefs. So what do you think of the state of one who received knowledge directly from him whose light filled the entire earth, nay, from him whose light is the source of all lights, and all intellects are in relation to his intellect like one who took a pebble...
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a historical proof that the Companions were not muqallid but followed based on clear evidence. The author begins by noting that even non-Arab pagans fiercely defended their ancestral religion with sword and death, only converting after clear truth was established. How much more the Arabs, known for their zealousness? He then recounts a specific incident: some Bedouins demanded a sign (aya) from the Prophet, and he provided a miracle that constituted a clear proof. The Bedouins, being native Arabic speakers, fully understood the implications. The Qur'an itself is filled with countless proofs. Moreover, the Prophet, the greatest teacher and most eloquent, spent thirteen years before any warfare, clarifying and establishing proofs until only the obstinate remained. The author argues that even the smallest amount of such teaching, when imparted by the Prophet to even the dullest learner, would completely remove taqlid from that person's beliefs. How much more, then, the Companions who learned directly from the Prophet, whose light fills the earth and whose intellect is incomparably superior? Thus, it is inconceivable that the Companions were muqallid.

تقليد
حجة
أعراب
آية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Companions accepted faith without proof or were simply following tradition.
Correction: The author shows that the Companions and even Bedouins demanded and received clear evidences from the Prophet, and the Prophet spent years teaching proofs, so their faith was based on evidence, not blind imitation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how long did the Prophet teach without warfare to establish proofs?
A) 10 years
B) 13 years
C) 23 years
D) 7 years

Key Takeaway
The Companions followed Islam based on clear proofs and miraculous signs, not blind imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Bedouins demanded a clear sign before believing. When have you required a clear evidence for your faith from Allah? Are there beliefs you hold simply because you were raised with them, without seeking proof? What would it take for you to be like those Bedouins—wholeheartedly convinced through evidence?
?
The Prophet spent thirteen years teaching without fighting, patiently clarifying proofs. Who in your life is waiting for you to patiently explain the truth to them? Are you willing to invest years of gentle proof-giving, as the Prophet did, or do you expect quick results? What is stopping you from being that kind of teacher?
?
Even a small amount of teaching from the Prophet removed all blind following from the dullest learner. You claim to be a follower of his message—does your faith rest on solid proof, or are you still imitating others? If your faith were tested like the Companions', would you be able to defend it with clear evidence, or would you falter? What one step can you take today to turn your taqlid into yaqin (certainty)?
