Why Early Muslims Didn't Need Kalam
Sanusi contrasts early believers with later generations, explaining the need for kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early Muslims did not engage in detailed theological debates and why later generations must study kalam to protect their faith.

Core Idea
The light of prophethood made doubts vanish; today we must strive to learn.

Sanusi explains that the companions lived in a time of prophetic light, where doubts and hidden diseases did not exist. But our era is filled with innovations and confusion, making the study of kalam essential for survival of faith. This passage sets the stage for why systematic theology is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the vivid contrasts Sanusi draws between the two eras.
Pay attention to the metaphors like 'white hair on a black bull'.
2
Identify the two groups of people in the prophetic era
Sanusi says people were either believing saints or unbelieving wretches. There was no middle ground of confusion.
This shows the clarity of that time.
3
Contrast with the current situation
Note how Sanusi describes the rarity of Sunnah, the prevalence of innovations, and the low state of most people's belief.
He mentions compound ignorance and corrupt belief.
4
Understand the remedy
The remedy is striving to learn from deeply-rooted scholars, despite their scarcity. Otherwise, one may die upon innovation unknowingly.
This justifies the study of kalam.
5
Reflect on the reasons for decline
Sanusi lists signs of the Hour, scarcity of scholars, and impostors as causes. This connects to the urgency of learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاية الأمر : أَنَّ القومَ الذين شاهدوه رضيَ اللهُ عنهم لَمَّا أَنْ أَشْرَقَتْ عليهم أنوار النبوَّةِ ، وتلاشَتْ معها ظلمات الجهل والوسواس ، وخَمَدَتْ عندَها نيران شياطين الإنس والجن .. لم ينبهوا صريحاً على دقائقِ الشُّبَهِ وخفيَّاتِ الأمراض التي ابتُلِيَ بها مَنْ بعدَهم ؛ لأنَّها لم تطرق منيع ساحتِهم ، ولا حَلَّتْ برفيع جُوارِهم ، ولا لاحَ قَزَعُها في صفاء شمسهم وارتفاع نهارهم وإنَّما الناسُ في ذلك الزمانِ أحد رجلين : مؤمن ولي ، أو كافر شقي ، وأما أزمنتنا هذهِ فالسنة فيها بين البدع كالشعرة البيضاء في جلد الثورِ الأسودِ ، فمَنْ لم يجاهدِ اليوم نفسَهُ في تعلم العلم وأخذِهِ من العلماء الراسخين - وما أندر اليوم وجودهم وأعزّ لقاءَهم ! - مات على أنواع مِنَ البدع والكفريات وهو لا يشعر لا سيما في هذا العلم وأكثرُ عامَّةِ الناس اليوم ليسَ في درجةِ الاعتقاد التقليدي المطابق ، بل في درجة الاعتقادِ الفاسد والجهل المركَبِ ، وما ذاكَ إِلا لقُرْبِ هجوم أشراط الساعة الكبرى ، وقِلَّةِ العلماء العاملين ، وانعدام المتعلمين الصادقينَ الفَطِنينَ ، وكثرة أبناء الدنيا المعجَبينَ بآرائهم الضالِّينَ المضلّينَ ، وتعرُّض الدجاجلة ممَّن انتمى إلى الرهبانية على غيرِ أصلِ علم لقطع طريقِ السنَّةِ بحبائلَ نصبوها مزخرفةٍ مِنْ حبائل مَرَدَةِ الشياطينِ ، نسأله سبحانه حسن الخاتمة بفضله وكرمه
The upshot is: that the people who witnessed him (may Allah be pleased with them) when the lights of prophethood shone upon them, and the darkness of ignorance and whispers vanished, and the fires of the devils of mankind and jinn were extinguished... they did not explicitly alert to the subtleties of doubts and hidden diseases with which those after them were afflicted; because those things did not assail their impregnable domain, nor did they settle in their lofty precincts, nor did their clouds appear in the clarity of their sun and the height of their day. And the people in that time were only two kinds: a believing saint (mu'min wali) or an unbelieving wretch (kafir shaqi). As for our times, the Sunnah among innovations is like a white hair on a black bull. Whoever does not strive today against his own soul in learning knowledge and taking it from the deeply-rooted scholars (and how rare their existence today and how precious their meeting!) dies upon kinds of innovations and disbeliefs without feeling it, especially in this science. And most common people today are not at the level of sound taqlid (taqlid muṭābiq), but at the level of corrupt belief (i'tiqād fāsid) and compound ignorance (jahl murakkab). That is only because of the near arrival of the great portents of the Hour, the scarcity of acting scholars, the lack of sincere and intelligent seekers, the abundance of worldly-minded people who are conceited with their opinions, misguided and misguiding, and the exposure to impostors who claimed to asceticism without any basis of knowledge to cut off the path of the Sunnah with ornate snares they set up from the snares of the rebellious devils. We ask Him, glorified, for a good end by His grace and generosity.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage contrasts the spiritual state of the early companions with that of later generations, especially the author's own time. The companions were so illuminated by prophethood that they were not exposed to subtle doubts and hidden spiritual diseases; they were either pure believers or open disbelievers. In contrast, the author's era is one where the Sunnah is rare among innovations, like a white hair on a black bull. The only way to avoid dying upon innovation and disbelief is to strive in learning true knowledge from the few remaining deeply-rooted scholars. Most common people today have a corrupt belief or compound ignorance, not even a sound taqlid. This is due to the approach of the signs of the Hour, the scarcity of acting scholars, the lack of sincere students, the abundance of misguided worldly people, and the intrigues of impostors who falsely claim asceticism. The passage ends with a prayer for a good end.

Key Terms
أنوار النبوة
البدع
الاعتقاد التقليدي
الاعتقاد الفاسد
الجهل المركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think kalam was needed in every era equally, or that early Muslims debated theology as we do.
Correction: The early Muslims did not face the subtle doubts and innovations of later times, so they did not need detailed kalam; we do.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what was the spiritual state of the people during the prophetic era?
A) They were all engaged in deep theological discussions
B) They were either believing saints or unbelieving wretches
C) They were mostly confused about their faith
D) They struggled to distinguish Sunnah from innovation

Key Takeaway
The prophetic era was purely illuminated; our era requires diligent study of kalam to preserve faith from innovations and doubts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi says the Sunnah among innovations is like a white hair on a black bull. Have you ever truly felt the rarity of authentic Sunnah in your own community? What specific, uncomfortable changes would you need to make in your daily life to ensure you are following the Sunnah and not the innovations that surround you?
?
The passage warns that most people today are in corrupt belief and compound ignorance, unaware of their own state. If you were to honestly examine your own theological knowledge right now, could you confidently say you are not among them? What concrete step will you take this week to move from assumption to certainty in your faith?
?
The early companions needed no kalam because doubts never touched them. But you live in a time where doubts are everywhere, and impostors masquerade as ascetics. When was the last time a doubt about your faith genuinely disturbed you? How does this lesson compel you to arm yourself with knowledge, and what will you do starting today to seek out a deeply-rooted scholar?

The Struggle for True Knowledge
Sanusi exhorts the seeker of knowledge with a metaphor and warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's urgent call to seek knowledge from true scholars and the extreme rarity of such scholars in his time.

Core Idea
True knowledge requires struggle against the self and finding rare deeply-rooted scholars.

Sanusi opens with a striking metaphor and immediately turns to a heartfelt exhortation. He warns that without a sincere effort to learn from the true scholars—who are now incredibly rare—one risks dying in a state of ignorance and innovation. This passage sets the tone for the entire work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to absorb the author's tone and main point.
Notice the opening metaphor 'skin of the black bull'—its exact meaning is debated, but it signals a strong statement.
2
Reflect on the metaphor
Consider why the author uses such a striking image. What does it convey about rarity or value?
The metaphor likely underscores the preciousness and difficulty of finding true knowledge.
3
Understand the warning
Identify the consequence of not struggling to learn from deeply-rooted scholars: dying upon innovations and disbeliefs without realizing it.
The warning is especially for 'this science' (kalam or theology).
4
Internalize the call
Ask yourself: What does 'struggle against the soul' mean in the context of seeking knowledge? How can you apply this today?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جلد الثورِ الأسودِ ، فمَنْ لم يجاهدِ اليوم نفسَهُ في تعلم العلم وأخذِهِ من العلماء الراسخين - وما أندر اليوم وجودهم وأعزّ لقاءَهم ! - مات على أنواع مِنَ البدع والكفريات وهو لا يشعرُ ولا سيما في هذا العلم وأكثرُ عامَّةِ الناس اليوم ليسَ في درجةِ الاعتقاد التقليدي المطابق ، بل في درجة الاعتقادِ الفاسد والجهل المركَبِ ، وما ذاكَ إِلا لقُرْبِ هجوم أشراط الساعة الكبرى ، وقِلَّةِ العلماء العاملين ، وانعدام المتعلمين الصادقينَ الفَطِنينَ ، وكثرة أبناء الدنيا المعجَبينَ بآرائهم الضالِّينَ المضلّينَ ، وتعرُّض الدجاجلة ممَّن انتمى إلى الرهبانية على غيرِ أصلِ علم لقطع طريقِ السنَّةِ بحبائلَ نصبوها مزخرفةٍ مِنْ حبائل مَرَدَةِ الشياطينِ ، نسأله سبحانه حسن الخاتمة بفضله وكرمه
The skin of the black bull. Whoever does not struggle today against his soul in learning knowledge and taking it from the deeply-rooted scholars — how rare is their existence today and how precious is meeting them! — will die upon types of innovations and disbeliefs while he does not perceive, especially in this science. And most of the common people today are not in the degree of correct traditional belief, but rather in the degree of corrupt belief and compounded ignorance. That is only due to the near approach of the major signs of the Hour, the scarcity of acting scholars, the absence of truthful and intelligent learners, the abundance of worldly people who are impressed with their own opinions, the misguided and misguiding, and the intrusion of charlatans from those who claim to monasticism without a basis of knowledge to cut off the path of the Sunnah with decorative snares they have set up from the snares of rebellious devils. We ask Him, exalted, for a good end by His grace and generosity.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a passionate lament and warning from the author. It opens with a striking metaphor ('the skin of the black bull'), likely a proverbial expression, then immediately calls the reader to jihad against the self in seeking knowledge from reliable scholars, noting their extreme rarity. The author warns that without this effort, one may die in a state of innovation and disbelief without realizing it. He then describes the current state of the common people: they have fallen below even correct taqlid into corrupt belief and compounded ignorance. The causes are listed: 1) the approach of the major signs of the Hour, 2) scarcity of acting scholars, 3) absence of sincere and intelligent students, 4) prevalence of worldly people who are deluded by their own opinions and lead others astray, and 5) the intrusion of deceptive pseudo-monastics who set up ornate snares to block the path of the Sunnah, inspired by devils. The passage concludes with a prayer for a good end. The tone is urgent and somber, setting the stage for the doctrinal discussions to follow.

Key Terms
البدع
الكفريات
العلماء الراسخين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can achieve salvation without seeking knowledge from true scholars.
Correction: Sanusi warns that without struggling to learn from deeply-rooted scholars, one risks dying upon innovations and disbeliefs.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Struggling to learn from true scholars is essential to avoid dying in ignorance and innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Deeply-rooted scholars are described as rare and their meeting precious. How hard are you searching for such a teacher? Name one concrete step you will take this week to find and learn from someone truly knowledgeable in this science.

The State of the People and the Signs of the Hour
Sanusi diagnoses the state of the common people and lists causes of deviation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's diagnosis of the widespread corruption of belief among common people and the five causes he identifies for this decline.

Core Idea
Most people have fallen into compounded ignorance due to approaching signs of the Hour and lack of sincere scholars.

After the initial warning, Sanusi describes the grim reality of his time: most common people do not even have correct taqlid, let alone certainty; they are in corrupt belief and compounded ignorance. He then lists five reasons for this, from the approach of the major signs to the intrusion of deceptive charlatans. This passage provides a sociological and eschatological analysis of religious decline.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English translation to get an overview of the content.
Notice the shift from the previous exhortation to a description of the state of society.
2
Identify the state of the common people
Find what Sanusi says about 'most common people' regarding their belief. They are not in correct traditional belief but in corrupt belief and compounded ignorance.
This is a strong claim about the depth of deviation.
3
List the five causes
The passage lists five causes introduced by 'due to': 1) Approach of major signs of the Hour, 2) Scarcity of acting scholars, 3) Absence of truthful learners, 4) Abundance of worldly misleaders, 5) Intrusion of charlatans.
Cause 5 mentions 'decorative snares' from devils.
4
Connect to the prayer
After listing the grim situation, Sanusi concludes with a prayer for a good end. Consider why he ends this way.
The prayer shows reliance on Allah's grace despite the dire circumstances.

And most of the common people today are not in the degree of correct traditional belief, but rather in the degree of corrupt belief and compounded ignorance. That is only due to the near approach of the major signs of the Hour, the scarcity of acting scholars, the absence of truthful and intelligent learners, the abundance of worldly people who are impressed with their own opinions, the misguided and misguiding, and the intrusion of charlatans from those who claim to monasticism without a basis of knowledge to cut off the path of the Sunnah with decorative snares they have set up from the snares of rebellious devils. We ask Him, exalted, for a good end by His grace and generosity.

Commentary
This passage is a passionate lament and warning from the author. It opens with a striking metaphor ('the skin of the black bull'), likely a proverbial expression, then immediately calls the reader to jihad against the self in seeking knowledge from reliable scholars, noting their extreme rarity. The author warns that without this effort, one may die in a state of innovation and disbelief without realizing it. He then describes the current state of the common people: they have fallen below even correct taqlid into corrupt belief and compounded ignorance. The causes are listed: 1) the approach of the major signs of the Hour, 2) scarcity of acting scholars, 3) absence of sincere and intelligent students, 4) prevalence of worldly people who are deluded by their own opinions and lead others astray, and 5) the intrusion of deceptive pseudo-monastics who set up ornate snares to block the path of the Sunnah, inspired by devils. The passage concludes with a prayer for a good end. The tone is urgent and somber, setting the stage for the doctrinal discussions to follow.

Key Terms
الاعتقاد التقليدي
الجهل المركب
أشراط الساعة
الدجاجلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The decline in religious knowledge is temporary and not linked to the signs of the Hour.
Correction: Sanusi directly attributes the corruption of belief to the near approach of the major signs of the Hour.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the state of most common people regarding belief?
A) They have correct traditional belief.
B) They are in corrupt belief and compounded ignorance.
C) They are all scholars.
D) They are all innovators.

Key Takeaway
The widespread corruption of belief is a sign of the Hour and stems from the scarcity of true scholars and the proliferation of deceivers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi mentions 'the absence of truthful and intelligent learners.' In your pursuit of knowledge, are you truthful about your intentions and intelligent in seeking the right teachers? Or do you follow those who are 'impressed with their own opinions'? Examine who you learn from and why.
?
He says 'most of the common people today are in compounded ignorance.' How have you contributed to this state in your own circle? Are you part of the solution by being a sincere seeker of truth, or part of the problem by neglecting knowledge or spreading misinformation?
?
The signs of the Hour are near. Does this reality shape your daily choices and priorities? Are you preparing for the end by seeking true knowledge and acting upon it, or are you distracted by worldly concerns? What one change will you make today to align with the path of the acting scholars?

The Permissibility of Kalam Terminological Innovations
Sanusi defends terminological innovation as permissible and following the Qur'anic method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why kalam scholars' use of new terminology is not a blameworthy innovation but a continuation of the Qur'anic method.

Core Idea
Terminological innovation is permissible when it serves the religion.

Sanusi addresses a common criticism: that kalam scholars introduced foreign concepts. He argues their method mirrors the Qur'an's own approach of citing false doubts then refuting them with decisive proofs. The new terminologies are merely tools to meet the needs of their time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Note the negation 'lam yazid' (did not add) which is implied despite OCR issue.
2
Identify the two-part defense
Sanusi first argues that their method follows the Qur'anic method of citing falsehoods then refuting them. Then he states that new terminologies are permissible and there is no consensus against them.
The phrase 'la hajra ijma'an' is key: it means 'no prohibition by consensus'.
3
Reflect on the principle
Think about why this argument matters: it shows that using new words or concepts in theology is not bid'a (innovation) if it helps preserve correct doctrine.
This connects to the broader principle of means being judged by their ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَزِدْ علماءُ الكلامِ مِنْ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ في كتبهم الكلامية شيئاً على نَهْجِ القرآنِ ؛ مِنْ حكاية الأقوال الفاسدة وشبهها ، ثم ذكرِ البراهين القطعية لإبطالها . وقصارى الأمرِ : أنَّهم أحدثوا اصطلاحاتٍ تليقُ بضبط العلم لأهلِ الزمان ، ولا حَجْرَ إجماعاً في الأوضاع والعباراتِ والتصرف فيها بحسَبِ ما يليقُ بمصالح الأقضية النازلاتِ
The scholars of kalam from the people of the Sunnah did not add anything in their kalam books beyond the method of the Qur'an: from narrating corrupt statements and their doubts, then mentioning decisive proofs for their invalidation. In short: they introduced terminologies suitable for organizing the knowledge for the people of the time, and there is no prohibition by consensus in the formulations and expressions and disposing of them according to what suits the interests of the cases that occur.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the kalam scholars' methodology. It begins by asserting that they did not depart from the Qur'anic approach; rather, their method involves citing corrupt sayings and their accompanying doubts, then presenting decisive proofs (al-barahin al-qat'iyya) to refute them. This aligns with the Qur'an's own method of reporting falsehoods and then disproving them. The author then summarizes that the scholars only innovated technical terminologies (istilahat) that help organize the science for their contemporaries, and there is no consensus-based prohibition (la hajra ijma'an) against new formulations and expressions, as long as they serve the needs of emerging legal cases. The key point is that terminological innovation is not religious innovation (bid'a) but a necessary tool for preserving the faith.

Key Terms
نهج القرآن
براهين قطعية
اصطلاحات
لا حجر إجماعاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Using philosophical terms in theology is a blameworthy innovation.
Correction: Sanusi argues that such terminology is permissible and even necessary, following the Qur'anic method of citing falsehoods then refuting them.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did kalam scholars introduce new terminologies?
A) To deviate from the Qur'anic method
B) To organize knowledge for their time, which is permissible by consensus
C) To imitate the philosophers
D) To make the religion difficult

Key Takeaway
Kalam scholars' use of new terminology is not an innovation in religion but a practical necessity, and it follows the Qur'anic method of citing falsehoods before refuting them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you were in a debate today and someone used a term like 'decisive proofs' or 'corrupt statements' in a way that felt foreign, would your heart trust that they are following the method of the Qur'an, or would your ego react defensively? How can you train yourself to judge by substance rather than by vocabulary?

The Necessity of Rational Inquiry for Understanding Revelation
Sanusi refutes the claim that only Quran and Sunnah are permissible sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational inquiry (nazar aqli) is not merely permissible but essential for establishing the authority of the Quran and Sunnah and for correctly interpreting ambiguous passages.

Core Idea
Reason is the key that unlocks the authority and meaning of revelation.

Sanusi here addresses a common objection: that Muslims should only rely on the Quran and Sunnah and shun rational inquiry. He turns the argument on its head by showing that without reason, the very proof of revelation cannot be known, and without sound reasoning, apparent meanings of scripture can lead to serious error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the structure: Sanusi presents a claim, then a refutation with two numbered points.
The passage is dense; take your time to absorb the logic.
2
Identify the two arguments of the refutation
The refutation consists of two distinct arguments, marked by (1) and (2). Write them down in your own words.
The first argument is about the proof of revelation; the second about the interpretation of ambiguous texts.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: If rational inquiry were truly forbidden, how would we know the Quran is from God? How would we understand verses that appear to describe God in physical terms?
This shows that reason is not an enemy but a servant of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا مَنْ زعم أنَّ الطريقَ بَدْءاً إلى معرفة الحق . . الكتاب والسنة ، ويحرم ما سواهما .. فالردُّ عليهِ : أَنَّ حُجَّتهما لا تُعرَفُ إلا بالنظر العقلي (١) ، وأيضاً فقد وقعَتْ فيهما ظواهرُ من اعتقدها على ظاهرها .. كفر وابتدع (۲) ، ولا يُحسِنُ تأويلها إلا الراسخ في علوم النظر ، المرتاضُ في عِلْمَي اللسان والبلاغة
As for one who claims that the path to knowledge of the truth from the beginning is the Book and the Sunnah, and that what is other than them is forbidden—the refutation of him is: that their proof is not known except through rational consideration (1). Also, there have occurred in them apparent meanings; whoever believes them according to their apparent meaning has disbelieved and innovated (2). And none excels in interpreting them except the firmly grounded in the sciences of consideration, the practiced in the two sciences of linguistics and rhetoric.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who argue that the only legitimate source for knowing the truth is the Quran and Sunnah, and that any rational inquiry beyond them is forbidden. Sanusi provides two counterarguments. First, the very authority of the Quran and Sunnah (their proof as divine revelation) cannot be known except through rational consideration (nazar aqli). That is, reason is needed to establish that these texts are indeed from God. Second, there are verses and hadiths that, if taken literally, lead to disbelief (kufr) and innovation (bid'a). Their proper interpretation (ta'wil) requires deep knowledge of rational sciences ('ulum al-nazar) and expertise in linguistics and rhetoric. Thus, prohibiting rational inquiry would leave these texts misunderstood and lead to error.

Key Terms
النظر العقلي
ظواهر
تأويل
الراسخ في علوم النظر
المرتاض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accepting the Quran and Sunnah requires no prior rational thought; one should simply submit without reasoning.
Correction: Sanusi shows that even the authority of the Quran and Sunnah is known through rational proof. Reason is not opposed to faith but is a necessary tool for establishing and understanding faith.

Checkpoint
What is the first reason Sanusi gives against prohibiting rational inquiry?
A) The Quran itself commands rational thought.
B) The authority of the Quran and Sunnah cannot be known without rational proof.
C) The Companions used reason in deriving rulings.
D) The Sunnah is incomplete without reason.

Key Takeaway
Rational inquiry is not an optional extra but a necessary tool for both establishing and understanding divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Have you ever dismissed rational inquiry as unnecessary or even harmful in your faith? How does Sanusi's argument challenge that assumption, and what will you change about your approach to learning Islam from now on?

Refutation of Spiritual Discipline as the Sole Path to Knowledge
Sanusi refutes the claim that spiritual discipline alone leads to knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that knowledge of God must precede any spiritual practice, and that rational consideration (nazar) is the foundation of faith.

Core Idea
Spiritual discipline deepens knowledge, but cannot produce it from nothing.

In this passage, Sanusi confronts a common claim: that rigorous spiritual discipline alone can lead to knowledge of God. He defines such discipline and then poses several pressing questions that reveal its dependency on prior knowledge. While he acknowledges the value of discipline after faith, he places it as a secondary branch, with rational inquiry as the root.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the literal translation. Notice how Sanusi structures his refutation.
The passage has two main parts: a refutation and a concession.
2
Identify the main refutation
Find the definition of spiritual discipline and the four rhetorical questions. Each question highlights a prerequisite that discipline cannot supply.
The questions are: worship without object, remembrance without subject, piety without commander, seeking permissible without permitter.
3
Understand the concession
Sanusi does not reject discipline entirely. He affirms its value for deepening knowledge and for ascending from faith to excellence—but only after knowledge of God is established.
4
Grasp the final priority
The last sentence makes the logical priority clear: the quest for higher states (branches) depends on first acquiring the foundation of faith through rational consideration (nazar).
Nazar is the root; spiritual discipline is a branch.
5
Reflect on the error corrected
The common misunderstanding is that discipline alone brings knowledge. This passage shows that discipline is a tool for growth, not a source of initial knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا مَنْ زعمَ أنَّ طريق المعرفةِ الرياضة والمجاهدة وتصفية الباطن .. فيُقالُ لهُ : الرياضةُ عبارةٌ عن ملازمة العزلة والخلوة وتناول الحلال ، والجوع ، والتقلُّلِ مِنَ الدنيا على سبيل الزهد فيها ، ومداومة التعبدِ والذكرِ ، وكيف يمكن التعبُّدُ لمَنْ لا يعرفُ معبودَهُ ؟! والذكرُ لمَنْ لا يعرفُ مذكورَهُ ؟! والتقوى لمَنْ لا يعرفُ آمَرَهُ وناهيَهُ ؟ ! أو طلب مباح لمَنْ لا يعرفُ المبيحَ ؟! نعم ؛ لا ننكرُ أنَّ الاستعانة بذلك بعد معرفة الله تعالى ، وإحكام ما يتقرَّبُ بِهِ إِليهِ .. سبب لرسوخ المعرفة والزيادة في المعارفِ وتَعرُّضُ لكثير مِنَ المواهب ، وللتري [؟] مِنْ مَقامِ الإِيمَانِ إِلى مَقامِ الإحسانِ ، فالبحثُ على ذلك فرع تحصيل أصل الإيمان بالنظر
As for one who claims that the path of knowledge is spiritual discipline, striving, and purification of the inner self—it is said to him: Spiritual discipline consists of adhering to seclusion and solitude, consuming lawful food, hunger, reducing worldly possessions in the way of renunciation, and continuous worship and remembrance. And how can one worship when he does not know his object of worship?! And how can one remember when he does not know what he remembers?! And how can one have piety when he does not know who commands and prohibits him?! Or how can one seek what is permissible when he does not know who permits?! Yes, we do not deny that seeking help through these practices after knowledge of God Most High and perfecting what one draws near to Him with is a cause for the deepening of knowledge, increase in cognitions, and exposure to many gifts, and for [ascending?] from the station of faith to the station of excellence. So the quest for that is a branch of acquiring the foundation of faith through consideration.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage refutes those who claim that spiritual discipline (riyada), striving (mujahada), and inner purification alone lead to knowledge of God. Sanusi defines spiritual discipline as consisting of seclusion, eating lawful food, hunger, renunciation, constant worship and remembrance. He then poses rhetorical questions: how can one worship without knowing the object of worship? How can one remember without knowing the one remembered? How can one have piety without knowing the commander and prohibitor? How can one seek the permissible without knowing the permitter? These questions show that knowledge of God must precede these practices. However, Sanusi clarifies that he does not deny that after acquiring knowledge of God and mastering acts of devotion, such practices can deepen knowledge and elevate one from the station of faith to the station of excellence (ihsan). But the pursuit of those higher states is a branch (far') that depends on first acquiring the root (asl) of faith through rational consideration (nazar). Thus, rational inquiry is prior to spiritual discipline.

Key Terms
الرياضة
المجاهدة
تصفية الباطن
المعبود
النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spiritual discipline alone can lead to knowledge of God.
Correction: Sanusi shows that discipline presupposes knowledge of God; one cannot worship, remember, or obey without knowing the object. Rational consideration (nazar) must come first.

Checkpoint
What is Sanusi's main objection to those who claim spiritual discipline is the path to knowledge?
A) Spiritual discipline is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) One cannot worship or obey God without first knowing Him.
C) Spiritual discipline leads to arrogance.
D) Spiritual discipline is impossible without a teacher.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of God through rational consideration is the essential foundation; spiritual discipline builds upon it but cannot replace it.

Why Rational Reflection Is Necessary for Understanding Revelation
Sanusi refutes the claim that only Quran and Sunnah are valid paths to knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's two arguments refuting the claim that rational reflection is forbidden.

Core Idea
Reason is not opposed to revelation; it is required to even recognize revelation.

Some Muslims have argued that only the Quran and Sunnah are valid sources of knowledge, and that rational inquiry (nazar) is forbidden. Sanusi responds with a double refutation: first, the very authority of scripture depends on rational proof; second, scripture itself requires rational interpretation to avoid error. This lesson unpacks both arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once and then the English translation. Notice the two parts of the refutation marked by 'first' and 'also'.
The passage is compact; each sentence carries weight.
2
Examine the first argument
Sanusi argues that the proof (hujja) of the Quran and Sunnah is known only through rational reflection. Ask yourself: How does one know that the Quran is from God without using reason?
This establishes reason as a prerequisite for accepting revelation.
3
Examine the second argument
Sanusi points out that revelation contains apparent meanings (zawahir) that, if taken literally, lead to disbelief or innovation. Only those trained in rational sciences and linguistics can properly interpret them.
This shows that reason is needed even after accepting scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا مَنْ زعم أنَّ الطريقَ بَدْءاً إلى معرفة الحق . . الكتاب والسنة ، مَ ويحرم ما سواهما .. فالردُّ عليهِ : أَنَّ حُجَّتهما لا تُعرَفُ إلا بالنظر العقلي (١) ، وأيضاً فقد وقعَتْ فيهما ظواهرُ من اعتقدها على ظاهرها .. كفر وابتدع (۲) ، ولا يُحسِنُ تأويلها إلا الراسخ في علوم النظر ، المرتاضُ في عِلْمَي اللسان والبلاغة
And as for the one who claims that the beginning path to knowledge of the truth is only the Book and the Sunnah, and forbids anything other than them, the refutation against him is: that their proof is not known except through rational reflection (al-nazar al-'aqli), and also there have occurred in them apparent meanings (zawahir) that whoever believes them in their apparent sense becomes a disbeliever and an innovator, and no one can interpret them properly except the one deeply rooted in the sciences of reflection, trained in the two sciences of language and rhetoric.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that the only valid path to knowledge of divine truth is the Quran and Sunnah, and that rational inquiry (nazar) is forbidden. The author gives two arguments. First, the very proof (hujja) of the Quran and Sunnah is not known except through rational reflection—i.e., one must use reason to establish that the Quran is from God and that the Sunnah is authentic. Thus rational reflection is a prerequisite. Second, within revelation itself there are verses and hadiths whose apparent meanings (zawahir) if taken literally would lead to disbelief or innovation. Only someone who is deeply grounded ('rasikh') in the sciences of nazar (rational inquiry) and trained in linguistics and rhetoric can properly interpret such texts. Therefore rational reflection is not only permissible but necessary to avoid error.

Key Terms
النظر العقلي
الظواهر
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational inquiry (nazar) is opposed to revelation and should be avoided.
Correction: Sanusi shows that rational reflection is necessary both to establish the authority of revelation and to properly interpret its ambiguous texts.

B) Because the very authority of Quran and Sunnah is proven by rational reflection.
C) Because reason is superior to revelation.
D) Because the Quran commands rational reflection.

Key Takeaway
Rational reflection is not only permissible but necessary for properly understanding and authenticating revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Knowledge Must Precede Spiritual Practice
Sanusi refutes the claim that spiritual exercise alone suffices for knowledge of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational knowledge of Allah must precede any spiritual practice and why spiritual exercise alone cannot lead to true knowledge of God.

Core Idea
Spiritual practice without knowledge of God is blind worship.

Sanusi addresses a common misconception that rigorous spiritual exercises alone can bring one to knowledge of God. He defines such exercises and then asks penetrating questions that reveal their dependence on prior knowledge. This lesson examines his refutation and the importance of correct rational foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Try to grasp the overall flow before diving into analysis.
The passage is a continuous argument; note the rhetorical questions.
2
Identify the definition of riyada
Sanusi defines spiritual exercise (riyada) as seclusion, lawful food, hunger, asceticism, and continuous worship. Understand what is being refuted.
The definition sets the stage for his critique.
3
Analyze the rhetorical questions
Focus on the four questions: How can one worship without knowing the worshipped? Remember without knowing the remembered? Be pious without knowing the commander? Seek the permitted without knowing the permitter? These show that knowledge is prior to practice.
These questions are the core of the refutation.
4
Understand the warnings
Notice Sanusi's acknowledgment that practices help after knowledge, but warn against premature pursuit. He gives the example of Brahmins and Christians and warns about satanic deception.
This section shows the dangers of engaging in spiritual exercise without correct foundation.

وأَمَّا مَنْ زعمَ أنَّ طريق المعرفةِ الرياضة والمجاهدة وتصفية الباطن .. فيُقالُ لهُ : الرياضةُ عبارةٌ عن ملازمة العزلة والخلوة وتناول الحلال ، والجوع ، والتقلُّلِ مِنَ الدنيا على سبيل الزهد فيها ، ومداومة التعبدِ والذكرِ ، وكيف يمكن التعبُّدُ لمَنْ لا يعرفُ معبودَهُ ؟! والذكرُ لمَنْ لا يعرفُ مذكورَهُ ؟! والتقوى لمَنْ لا يعرفُ آمَرَهُ وناهيَهُ ؟ ! أو طلب مباح لمَنْ لا يعرفُ المبيحَ ؟! نعم ؛ لا ننكرُ أنَّ الاستعانة بذلك بعد معرفة الله تعالى ، وإحكام ما يتقرَّبُ بِهِ إِليهِ .. سبب لرسوخ المعرفة والزيادة في المعارفِ وتَعرُّضُ لكثير مِنَ المواهب ، وللتري مِنْ مَقامِ الإِيمَانِ إِلى مَقامِ الإحسانِ ، فالبحثُ على ذلك فرع تحصيل أصل الإيمان بالنظر الصحيح ، وتحصيل علوم يطولُ تتبعها ، والتقدم لمعالي الأمورِ قبل إتقان أصولها وضبْطِ طُرُقِها .. عجلة وشهوة نفسانيةٌ تُوجِبُ لصاحبها الفضيحة دنيا وأُخرى ، وإلا فالبراهمة والنصارى قد ارتاضوا على قاعدة فاسدة ، فلم يَزِدْهم ذلكَ إلا ضلالاً ، وكثيراً ما يغتر أصحاب هذا الطريق بالتخيلاتِ الشيطانيّةِ أو النفسانية نوماً ويقظةً ، ويَعُدُّونَها كرامات ، وهي في الحقيقة استدراج وزيادة لهم في أنواع الضَّلالاتِ ، نسألُهُ سبحانَهُ أنْ يلهمنا رشْدَ أنفسنا ، وسنتعرَّضُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ لذكرِ شروط الوليّ في فصْلِ النبوَّةِ ؛ عندَ بيانِ الفَرْقِ بين الكرامة والمعجزة(١)
And as for the one who claims that the path of knowledge is spiritual exercise (riyada), striving (mujahada), and purification of the inner self, it is said to him: spiritual exercise is the state of constant seclusion and retreat, consuming lawful food, hunger, reducing worldly possessions by way of asceticism, continuous worship and remembrance. How can worship be possible for one who does not know his worshipped? And remembrance for one who does not know his remembered? And piety for one who does not know his commander and prohibitor? Or seeking what is permitted for one who does not know the permitter? Yes, we do not deny that seeking help from these after knowledge of God Almighty and perfecting those things by which one draws near to Him is a cause for rootedness of knowledge, increase in knowledges, and exposure to many gifts, and for elevation from the station of faith to the station of excellence. So research on that is a branch of obtaining the foundation of faith through correct reflection, and obtaining sciences whose pursuit is lengthy. And advancing to lofty matters before mastering their principles and controlling their methods is haste and a carnal desire that brings disgrace to its possessor in this world and the next. Otherwise, the Brahmins and Christians have practiced spiritual exercise upon a corrupt foundation, so that did not increase them except in error. And often the followers of this path are deceived by satanic or psychological fantasies, asleep or awake, and consider them miracles, but in reality they are gradual entrapment and increase for them in types of misguidance. We ask Him, glorified be He, to inspire us with right guidance for ourselves. And we will, God willing, mention the conditions of the saint in the chapter on prophethood, when explaining the difference between miracle (karama) and miracle (mu'jiza).
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that the sole path to knowledge of God is spiritual exercise (riyada), striving (mujahada), and inner purification. The author defines riyada as seclusion, lawful food, hunger, asceticism, and constant worship and dhikr. He then poses rhetorical questions: how can one worship without knowing the object of worship? How can one remember without knowing the One remembered? How can one be pious without knowing the commander? How can one seek the permitted without knowing the permittor? Thus prior knowledge of God is essential. The author acknowledges that after acquiring sound knowledge of God, these practices are useful: they deepen knowledge, increase spiritual gifts, and elevate from the station of faith to the station of excellence (ihsan). However, he warns that engaging in these practices without first securing correct rational knowledge (nazar sahih) and mastering foundational sciences is premature and leads to disgrace. He cites the Brahmins and Christians who practiced asceticism on a false foundation and only increased in error. Furthermore, he cautions that many are deceived by satanic or psychological fantasies, mistaking them for miracles (karamat), whereas they are actually divine entrapment. The section ends with a note that the topic of sainthood and the distinction between miracles and extraordinary acts will be treated later.

Key Terms
الرياضة
المجاهدة
تصفية الباطن
الكرامة
الاستدراج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spiritual exercises alone can lead to knowledge of God without prior rational understanding.
Correction: Sanusi shows that one cannot worship, remember, or obey God without first knowing Him through correct rational reflection.

Checkpoint
What is Sanusi's main objection to those who claim spiritual exercise alone is the path to knowledge?
A) Such practices are forbidden in Islam.
B) One cannot worship God without first knowing Him through rational reflection.
C) Spiritual exercise is impossible without a teacher.
D) The practices lead to pride.

Key Takeaway
True knowledge of Allah must precede and guide all spiritual practices; without it, practices risk being empty or even deceptive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Consider any 'spiritual experiences' you have had or seek. How will you test them against the criteria of sound knowledge and the guidance of scholars, rather than assuming they are divine favors?

Refutation of Inspiration as the Sole Path to Knowledge
Sanusi refutes the claim that mere detachment and inspiration yield knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational reflection and pre-existing sciences are necessary for knowledge, and why inspiration alone is insufficient according to Sanusi.

Core Idea
Inspiration without reason is blind; knowledge requires prior sciences and reflection.

Sanusi engages with a claim attributed to certain Indian philosophers that true knowledge comes solely through inspiration, achieved by detaching the soul from bodily distractions. He argues that this view is incomplete because mere detachment cannot produce specific knowledge without prior sciences and rational reflection. This passage establishes the indispensability of nazar (rational inference) in the pursuit of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
Notice the structure: claim, explanation, refutation.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and its refutation
Find the part where Sanusi presents the Indian view and then his refutation. What is the key flaw he identifies?
The refutation hinges on 'مُجرَّدَ إزالة الشواغل' being insufficient.
3
Reflect on the role of nazar
Sanusi insists that nazar (reflection) and prior sciences are necessary. How does this challenge the idea of pure inspiration?
Consider why 'علوم' (sciences) are needed alongside detachment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَنْ قالَ مِنَ الهنودِ : إِنَّ طريق المعرفة الإلهام ، وعَنَوا بهِ : أَنَّ النفس إذا تَجرَّدَتْ للشيء وأزالَتِ الشواغل البدنية أدركَتْه ؛ فإنَّها في أصل خلقتِها مُستعِدَّةٌ لقَبولِ المعارفِ .. فالردُّ عليهم : أَنَّ مُجرَّدَ إزالة الشواغل لا يُحصِّلُ المطلوب الخاص إلا مع حضور علوم ؛ إمَّا ضرورية أو غير ضروريةٍ يَترتّب عليها المطلوب ؛ وهو النظر والتجريد لازمه (٢)
And someone from the Indians who said: the path of knowledge is inspiration (ilham), and they meant by it that when the soul becomes detached for a thing and removes bodily distractions, it perceives it; for it is in its original creation prepared to receive knowledge. So the refutation against them is that mere removal of distractions does not produce the specific sought result except with the presence of sciences; either necessary or non-necessary upon which the sought result depends; and it is reflection (al-nazar), and abstraction (al-tajrid) is necessary for it.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a claim attributed to some Indians that the path to knowledge is inspiration (ilham). They hold that when the soul detaches itself from bodily concerns and removes distractions, it can directly perceive truths, because the soul is inherently prepared to receive knowledge. The refutation is that mere removal of distractions (izalat al-shawaghib) does not by itself produce the specific knowledge sought. Rather, there must already be some sciences ('ulum')—either necessary (daruriyya) or acquired—that serve as premises from which the sought conclusion follows. The act of reflection (nazar) and abstraction (tajrid) are necessary to bring that knowledge. In other words, inspiration alone is insufficient; rational inference is required.

Key Terms
الإلهام
التجريد
النظر
الشواغل البدنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Inspiration alone, achieved by detaching from bodily distractions, can lead to true knowledge without any prior learning or rational effort.
Correction: Sanusi shows that mere removal of distractions is insufficient; one needs pre-existing sciences and rational reflection (nazar) to reach specific knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is mere removal of bodily distractions insufficient to attain true knowledge?
A) Because the soul is corrupt.
B) Because specific knowledge requires pre-existing sciences and rational reflection.
C) Because inspiration only comes through prophets.
D) Because the body is necessary for perception.

Key Takeaway
Mere detachment and inspiration cannot produce knowledge; rational reflection and prior sciences are essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This lesson shows that even the soul's detachment requires prior sciences. Where in your life have you neglected to build a foundation of knowledge, hoping that intuition would carry you? Will you commit to learning the necessary sciences, even if it is hard?

Warning against seeking high matters without fundamentals
Sanusi warns against seeking high matters without fundamentals and cautions against false spirituality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why seeking advanced spiritual knowledge without solid foundations leads to disgrace and how to distinguish true miracles from satanic delusions.

Core Idea
Spiritual shortcuts without fundamentals lead to disgrace, not sainthood.

Sanusi delivers a sharp warning to those who rush after lofty spiritual experiences and deep theological questions without first building a solid foundation in the basics. He points to the Brahmins and Christians as examples of how even sincere effort on a corrupt basis only increases error. Before you read the passage, consider: what might happen if someone tries to run before they can walk in their religious learning?

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the strong language Sanusi uses: 'disgrace', 'deluded', 'misguidance'.
The passage begins mid-sentence with 'الصحيح' – the context is that some people claim to have a shortcut to knowledge.
2
Identify the two main warnings
The passage contains two distinct warnings. Find them: first about rushing to high matters, second about mistaking satanic thoughts for miracles.
The examples of Brahmins and Christians support the first warning.
3
Reflect on the consequences
Consider what Sanusi says about the outcomes: disgrace in both worlds for the first, and 'istidraj' (gradual luring into sin) for the second. Ask yourself why this matters for your own learning.
Think about how this applies to modern seekers who chase spiritual experiences without proper grounding.

الصحيح ، وتحصيل علوم يطولُ تتبعها ، والتقدم لمعالي الأمورِ قبل إتقان أصولها وضبْطِ طُرُقِها .. عجلة وشهوة نفسانيةٌ تُوجِبُ لصاحبها الفضيحة دنيا وأُخرى ، وإلا فالبراهمة والنصارى قد ارتاضوا على قاعدة فاسدة ، فلم يَزِدْهم ذلكَ إلا ضلالاً ، وكثيراً ما يغتر أصحاب هذا الطريق بالتخيلاتِ الشيطانيّةِ أو النفسانية نوماً ويقظةً ، ويَعُدُّونَها كرامات ، وهي في الحقيقة استدراج وزيادة لهم في أنواع الضَّلالاتِ ، نسألُهُ سبحانَهُ أنْ يلهمنا رشْدَ أنفسنا ، وسنتعرَّضُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ لذكرِ شروط الوليّ في فصْلِ النبوَّةِ ؛ عندَ بيانِ الفَرْقِ بين الكرامة والمعجزة
The correct [path?], and the acquisition of sciences whose pursuit is lengthy, and advancing to lofty matters before mastering their foundations and controlling their methods is haste and a soul's desire that brings disgrace upon its possessor in this world and the next. Otherwise, the Brahmins and Christians have become accustomed to a corrupt foundation, and that only increased them in error. And many of the followers of this path are deceived by satanic or soulful imaginations, sleeping or waking, and count them as karamaat, while in reality they are a gradual luring and an increase for them in types of misguidance. We ask Him, glorified, to inspire us with the rightness of our souls. And we shall address, if God wills, the mention of the conditions of the wali in the chapter on prophethood, when clarifying the difference between karama and mu'jiza.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a warning against seeking high levels of knowledge and spiritual states without first mastering the fundamentals. The author begins by stating that advancing to lofty matters before mastering their foundations and controlling their methods is a form of haste and a soulful desire that brings disgrace in both worlds. He then gives examples: the Brahmins and Christians became accustomed to a corrupt foundation, so their efforts only increased them in error. He then notes that many who follow this path are deceived by satanic or soulful imaginations, interpreting them as karamaat (miraculous favors from God) when in fact they are a form of istidraaj (gradual luring into sin) and an increase in misguidance. The author ends with a prayer for guidance and a promise to later discuss the conditions of the wali (saint) and the difference between karama and mu'jiza.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that having spiritual experiences or strong inspirations is a sign of high spiritual rank, even without proper learning.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that such experiences may be satanic delusions or psychological projections, not true miracles, and that they can lead to further misguidance.

Checkpoint

A) It leads to success.
B) It brings disgrace in both worlds.

Key Takeaway
Advancing in religious knowledge without mastering its foundations leads to disgrace, and mistaking satanic delusions for miracles is a form of divine punishment, not blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Sanusi says that false spirituality only increases misguidance. Is there an area in your life where you rely on spiritual 'highs' rather than sound knowledge? What step will you take today to ensure your foundation is correct?

The Danger of Speaking Without Foundation
Sanusi warns against pretentious speakers and offers a supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the warning against speaking without proper knowledge and the importance of humility before Allah.

Core Idea
Speaking without foundation leads to deprivation from Allah's signs.

Sanusi concludes his discussion of methodology with a warning about pretentious speakers who argue without foundation. He then turns to supplication, asking Allah to include him among the successful. This lesson reflects on the danger of arrogance in seeking knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the shift from criticism to prayer.
2
Identify the two elements
The passage has two parts: a warning against pretentious speakers and a supplication. Identify how they connect.
The warning leads to the need for divine guidance.
3
Reflect on the Quranic verse
The verse from al-A'raf shows that arrogance causes one to be turned away from Allah's signs. Consider how this applies to learning.
This supports the author's point about deprivation.
4
Apply the lesson
Think about how this warning applies to students of knowledge. Why is humility important in seeking truth?

وهذا شأنُ المُتشدِّقينَ الخائضين فيما لا يعنيهم قبل ما يعنيهم ، وزادوا على العامة بالجدال في الباطل والتكثر عن الإنصاف للحقِّ ، ومِنْ ثَمَّ حُرموا ، سَأَصْرِفُ عَنْ ءَايَتِيَ الَّذِينَ يَتَكَبَّرُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٦] . اللهم ؛ أدخلنا في زمرة المفلحين في الدنيا والآخرة ، ولا تهلكنا مع الهالكين يا أرحم الراحمين .
And this is the condition of the pretentious speakers who plunge into what does not concern them before what concerns them. They added to the common people by arguing about falsehood and by increasing in number over fairness to the truth. Consequently, they were deprived. 'I will turn away from My signs those who are arrogant in the land without right' [al-Aʿrāf 7:146]. O Allah, include us among the successful in this world and the Hereafter, and do not destroy us with the destroyers, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage continues the criticism of those who speak without proper knowledge. The author describes them as 'al-mutashaddiqīn' (pretentious speakers) who delve into matters that do not concern them before mastering what does concern them. They surpass even the common people by arguing for falsehood and by amassing numbers rather than being fair to the truth. As a result, they are deprived of guidance, as indicated by the Quranic verse 'I will turn away from My signs those who are arrogant in the land without right.' The author then makes a supplication, asking Allah to include him among the successful and to save him from destruction.

The Truly Intelligent Person and the Need for Knowledge
Sanusi defines عاقل and stresses the need for divine grace and learning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi defines the truly intelligent person as one who acknowledges his own ignorance and dependence on divine grace for acquiring correct belief.

Core Idea
True intelligence begins with self-awareness and reliance on Allah's grace.

Sanusi opens by defining genuine intelligence as fairness to oneself. He stresses that even basic faith requires divine grace and mixing with knowledge. This lesson explores that foundational insight and the danger of ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Sanusi contrasts the intelligent person with the ignorant.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لولا فضله تعالى وتوفيقه'.
2
Identify the definition of عاقل
Find how Sanusi defines the truly intelligent person and what he criticizes about those who are ignorant of necessities.
3
Reflect on the role of divine grace
Consider why Sanusi says even scholars would not have perfected belief without divine grace and mixing with knowledge.
This connects to the broader theme of tawfiq.

والعاقل في الحقيقةِ مَنْ أنصفَ مِنْ نفسِهِ ، فوالله ؛ لولا فضله تعالى وتوفيقه لمخالطة العلم وأهلِهِ .. لَمَا كُنَّا نُحسِنُ عقائدَ الإِيمَانِ بِمُجرَّدِ التقليد فضلاً عن النظرِ ، ولكنَّا في أوديةٍ مِن اعتقاداتِ أهلِ الباطل نهيمُ ، وعجباً لعاقل يجهلُ الضروريَّاتِ ! حتى لم يشعر بحال نفسِهِ قبل مخالطة العلمِ ، ولا شعرَ بحالِ العوام ومَنْ أعرض عن النظرِ جملةً ولقد ألَّفَ علماء السنَّةِ رضي الله عنهم تواليف مختصرةً اقتصروا فيها على سرْدِ العقائدِ مُجرَّدةً عنِ الأدلَّةِ ؛ لتحفظها العامَّةُ ومَنْ قَصُرَ عقلُهُ عن النظرِ ، وليرتقوا مِنْ معرفتها تقليداً إلى البحث عن أدلَّتِها ، وما ذلك إلا لأنَّهم رأوا أكثرَ العامَّةِ لا تُحسِنُ العقائد ولو بالتقليد ، فأرادوا مِنْ نصيحتهم أن ينقلوهم مِنْ مرتبة يُخشى عليهم فيها أن يكونوا على اعتقادِ مُجمَع فيه على الكفر إلى مرتبة مُختلَفٍ فيها ، ولعلها تكونُ سُلَّماً إلى المعرفة . وبالجملة : فأهلُ النظرِ لم يصلوا كلُّهم إلى الحقِّ ، وَإِنَّما وصل القليلُ ، فكيفَ بمَنْ لم ينظرْ ؟! وما ذاك إلا لِمَا عُلِمَ أنَّ أحكام الوهم ورسوخ العوائدِ والمألوفاتِ تزاحم النظر الصحيحَ في هذا العلم مزاحمةً لا ينفكُ الحقُّ عنها إلا بعسر ليسَ فوقه عسر ، ولولا التوفيق الإلهي والتأييد الربَّانيُّ لَمَا أدركَ الخَلْقُ شيئاً مِنْ معرفةِ مَنْ لا تُكيَّفُهُ العقولُ ولا تَحُدُّهُ الأوهامُ ، لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ) [الشورى : 11]، ﴿ وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ مَا زَكَى مِنكُم مِّنْ أَحَدٍ أَبَدًا [النور : ٢١] .
The truly intelligent person is one who is fair to himself. For by Allah, were it not for His grace and success through mixing with knowledge and its people, we would not have been able to perfect the beliefs of faith by mere taqlid, let alone by speculation; rather we would be wandering in valleys of the beliefs of the people of falsehood. And it is amazing for an intelligent person to be ignorant of necessities! Until he is not aware of his own state before mixing with knowledge, nor is he aware of the state of the common people and those who turn away from speculation altogether. The Sunni scholars, may Allah be pleased with them, have composed short treatises in which they restricted themselves to listing creedal tenets stripped of proofs, so that the common people and those whose intellects are too short for speculation may memorize them, and so that they may ascend from knowing them by taqlid to researching their proofs. That is only because they saw that most common people do not perfect the beliefs even by taqlid. So they intended by their advice to transfer them from a rank in which it is feared they might hold a belief unanimously declared as disbelief to a rank in which there is disagreement, and perhaps it may be a ladder to knowledge. In summary: the people of speculation did not all reach the truth; only a few reached it. So what about those who did not speculate? That is because it is known that the judgments of illusion (wahm) and the deep-seatedness of habits and customs obstruct correct speculation in this science with an obstruction from which the truth is not freed except with difficulty above which there is no difficulty. And were it not for divine success and divine support, the creation would not have attained anything of the knowledge of Him whom intellects cannot qualify and illusions cannot limit. 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, All-Seeing' (Ash-Shura 42:11), 'And were it not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy, none of you would ever be purified' (An-Nur 24:21).
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy discussion on the virtue of scholars and the importance of learning for the common people. The author begins by defining the truly intelligent person as one who is fair to himself, acknowledging the grace of Allah in being able to mix with knowledge and its people. Without that, even the author claims they would not have perfected the beliefs of faith by taqlid (blind imitation), let alone by proper speculation; rather, they would be lost in the beliefs of falsehood. He then criticizes those who are ignorant of necessities—things that are intuitively known—and are unaware of their own state before learning. This leads to the point that Sunni scholars have written concise works that only list creedal statements without proofs, so that the common people can memorize them and gradually ascend from taqlid to seeking proofs. The reason is that most common people do not even perform taqlid correctly, and it is feared they might hold a belief that is unanimously considered kufr (disbelief). By memorizing these creeds, they move to a level where there is disagreement among scholars about the status of such belief, perhaps serving as a ladder to true knowledge. The author then summarizes that even among those who engage in speculation (ahl al-nazar), only a few reach the truth, so how about those who do not speculate at all? The difficulty is that false judgments of wahm (illusion/imagination) and deeply ingrained habits and customs obstruct correct speculation severely. Without divine grace (tawfiq) and support, no one can attain knowledge of Allah, who is beyond qualification by intellects and limitation by illusions. The passage ends with two Quranic verses affirming the uniqueness of Allah and the necessity of His grace for purification.

Key Terms
عاقل
توفيق
تقليد
عامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that taqlid is always sufficient without any prior knowledge or divine grace.
Correction: Sanusi shows that even taqlid requires divine grace and basic knowledge; without these, one cannot perfect belief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the truly intelligent person do?
A) Relies solely on his own intellect.
B) Is fair to himself and acknowledges his need for divine grace.
C) Avoids mixing with scholars.
D) Rejects taqlid entirely.

Key Takeaway
True intelligence means recognizing one's ignorance and dependence on Allah's grace for even basic faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truly fair to yourself? When was the last time you honestly admitted your ignorance about a matter of faith, rather than pretending to know? What would change if you made that confession today?
?
Sanusi says that without Allah's grace and mixing with knowledge, even he would be wandering in valleys of falsehood. Do you rely on your own intellect, or do you humbly seek knowledge from scholars and beg Allah for tawfīq? What is one step you can take this week to mix more deeply with knowledge and its people?
?
You consider yourself intelligent, but are you aware of your own state before you learned what you know? Have you ever thanked Allah for guiding you out of the darkness of ignorance? If not, pause now and reflect: if He had not guided you, where would you be?

The Scholars' Gift: Simplified Creeds for the Common People
Sanusi describes the scholars' composition of concise creeds and their purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunni scholars composed creedal summaries without proofs and how these serve as a ladder to deeper knowledge.

Core Idea
Simplified creeds lift the common people from danger of kufr toward true knowledge.

Sanusi explains the pedagogical wisdom of Sunni scholars who authored short treatises listing creedal statements without evidence. This lesson unpacks their motive: to help the masses memorize essential beliefs and eventually ascend to proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the purpose of the treatises and the scholars' observation about the common people.
2
Identify the three elements
Find the composition, the reason for it, and the intended goal (moving from one rank to another).
Look for 'لتحفظها', 'ليرتقوا', and 'ينقلوهم'.
3
Reflect on the ladder metaphor
Consider how memorizing a stripped creed can become a 'ladder to knowledge'.

Checkpoint
Why did the Sunni scholars write treatises without proofs?
A) To prevent the common people from using reason.
B) So the common people could memorize them and later ascend to seeking proofs.
C) To replace the Quran and Sunnah.
D) To confuse their opponents.

Key Takeaway
Concise creedal works are a ladder: they protect from kufr and lead to deeper inquiry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may have memorized a creed text like the 'Aqidah Tahawiyyah, but have you ever used it as a ladder to seek the proofs? Which rung are you on right now?
?
The scholars feared that common people might hold a belief unanimously considered kufr. Is your own understanding of faith based on sound knowledge, or are you content with a rank that could still be dangerous?
?
If you are in a position to teach others, are you giving them a tool for ascent, or just a security blanket that leaves them stuck in taqlid? What will you do to help them climb?

The Hard Path to Truth: Obstacles and Divine Grace
Sanusi highlights the difficulty of reaching truth and the necessity of divine grace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obstacles (illusion and habits) that obstruct correct speculation and why divine grace is absolutely necessary to know Allah.

Core Idea
Without divine grace, human efforts are trapped by illusion and custom.

Sanusi closes with a sobering reality: only a few speculators reach truth. He identifies the deep-seated obstacles of illusion (wahm) and ingrained habits, then emphasizes that divine grace and support are indispensable. This lesson delves into those barriers and the Quranic verses that affirm Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Notice the summary statement, then the description of obstacles, then the role of divine grace.
Pay attention to 'أحكام الوهم' and 'رسوخ العوائد'.
2
Analyze the obstacles
Identify what Sanusi says about wahm (illusion) and habits obstructing correct speculation.
3
Reflect on the Quranic verses
Consider how the verses support the point that without divine grace, no one can be purified or know Allah.

Source Text

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human reason alone can arrive at certain knowledge of Allah.
Correction: Sanusi insists that even the best speculators are hindered by illusion and habits, and only divine grace enables true knowledge.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi say obstructs correct speculation in this science?
A) Lack of books and teachers.
B) The judgments of illusion and deep-seated habits.
C) The common people's hostility.
D) The difficulty of Arabic.

Key Takeaway
Correct knowledge of Allah is only possible through divine grace, as human efforts are obstructed by illusion and habit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that your intellect alone could lead you to the truth about Allah, only to find yourself confused or misled? Where in your life are you currently trusting your own reasoning more than seeking Allah's grace? Will you make a specific du'a today asking for divine guidance in understanding Him?
?
What deeply ingrained habits or customs in your community—or in your own mind—prevent you from seeing the truth clearly? Are you willing to break free from them, even if it means discomfort or loneliness? What is one habit you will actively challenge this week?
?
This passage says that without Allah's grace, no one would ever be purified. Are you relying on your own efforts to purify your heart and beliefs, or are you constantly turning to Allah for help? What step will you take today to humble yourself and ask for His tawfiq in your journey of faith?

beginner
5 min
Why Scholars Restricted to Listing Doctrines without Proofs
Sanusi explains why some scholars omitted proofs and highlights the difficulty of attaining truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pedagogical and theological reasons why some scholars compiled creedal works without proofs, and the role of divine grace in attaining true knowledge.

Core Idea
Simplified creeds are a ladder from imitation to inquiry, but truth requires divine grace.

Sanusi addresses a common question: why do some books list doctrines without proofs? He explains that this method serves the common people and provides a stepping stone toward deeper investigation. But he also warns that even rigorous inquiry faces obstacles from imagination and habit, and that ultimate knowledge of Allah depends on divine assistance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi moves from a specific pedagogical point to a broader epistemological one.
2
Identify the first reason
Find where Sanusi explains the pedagogical benefit for the common people: why listing doctrines without proofs helps them memorize and ascend to inquiry.
3
Identify the second reason
Find where Sanusi shifts to the difficulty of attaining truth even for inquirers, and the obstacles of imagination and habit.
He concludes with the necessity of divine grace.
4
Reflect on the connection
Consider how these two reasons together form a complete justification: simplified works are both practical and humble in the face of divine mystery.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقتصروا فيها على سرْدِ العقائدِ مُجرَّدةً عنِ الأدلَّةِ ؛ لتحفظها العامَّةُ ومَنْ قَصُرَ عقلُهُ عن النظرِ ، وليرتقوا مِنْ معرفتها تقليداً إلى البحث عن أدلَّتِها ، وما ذلك إلا لأنَّهم رأوا أكثرَ العامَّةِ لا تُحسِنُ العقائد ولو بالتقليد ، فأرادوا مِنْ نصيحتهم أن ينقلوهم مِنْ مرتبة يُخشى عليهم فيها أن يكونوا على اعتقادِ مُجمَع فيه على الكفر إلى مرتبة مُختلَفٍ فيها ، ولعلها تكونُ سُلَّماً إلى المعرفة • وبالجملة : فأهلُ النظرِ لم يصلوا كلُّهم إلى الحقِّ ، وإِنَّما وصل القليلُ ، فكيفَ بمَنْ لم ينظرْ ؟! وما ذاك إلا لِمَا عُلِمَ أنَّ أحكام الوهم ورسوخ العوائدِ والمألوفاتِ تزاحم النظر الصحيحَ في هذا العلم مزاحمةً لا ينفكُ الحقُّ عنها إلا بعسر ليسَ فوقه عسر ، ولولا التوفيق الإلهي والتأييد الربَّانيُّ لَمَا أدركَ الخَلْقُ شيئاً مِنْ معرفةِ مَنْ لا تُكيَّفُهُ العقولُ ولا تَحُدُّهُ الأوهامُ ، لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ) [الشورى : 11]، ﴿ وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ مَا زَكَى مِنكُم مِّنْ أَحَدٍ أَبَدًا ﴾ [النور : ٢١]
They restricted themselves in it to listing doctrines stripped of proofs, so that the common people and those whose intellect is too short for inquiry may memorize them, and so that they may ascend from knowing them by imitation to searching for their proofs. That was only because they saw that most of the common people do not even properly hold doctrines even by imitation, so they wanted out of sincere advice to transfer them from a station where it is feared that they might be upon a belief unanimously deemed disbelief to a station where there is disagreement, and perhaps it may become a ladder to knowledge. In short: the people of inquiry did not all reach the truth; only a few reached it. How then with one who did not inquire? That is only because it is known that the judgments of imagination, the entrenchment of habits and familiar things, hinder correct inquiry in this science with a hindrance from which truth is not freed except with difficulty beyond which there is no difficulty. And were it not for divine success and lordly support, creation would not have attained anything of the knowledge of Him whom intellects cannot qualify and imaginations cannot limit. 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' (Shura 42:11); 'And if it were not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy, not one of you would ever have been purified' (Nur 24:21).
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage explains the pedagogical and theological reasoning behind works that list doctrines without proofs. Sanusi begins by stating that the purpose of such works is to allow the common people ('amma) and those intellectually unable to engage in rational inquiry (nazar) to memorize the doctrines, and then to gradually rise from mere imitation (taqlid) to investigating the proofs. He notes that most common people do not even properly hold the doctrines by imitation, so the scholars aimed to move them from a level where they might hold a belief that is unanimously deemed disbelief to a level where there is legitimate disagreement (perhaps meaning a level where they are at least not in clear error), and this might be a stepping stone to true knowledge. Then Sanusi broadens the point: even among the people of inquiry, few reach the truth. This is because imagination (wahm) and ingrained habits and familiar things (maw'ulufat) strongly obstruct correct inquiry in this science. Truth only emerges with great difficulty. He concludes that without divine grace and help, no one could attain knowledge of God, who is beyond human conceptualization. This emphasizes the necessity of divine assistance in acquiring true knowledge.

تقليد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Memorizing doctrines without proofs is sufficient for correct faith.
Correction: Such works are only a first step; the goal is to ascend to rational inquiry and rely on divine grace.

Why did some scholars write works listing only doctrines without proofs?
A) To encourage blind imitation without inquiry
B) To help the common people memorize and then gradually ascend to seeking proofs
C) Because they rejected rational proofs altogether
D) To hide the proofs from the public

Key Takeaway
Simplified creedal works are a practical pedagogical tool, but true knowledge of Allah ultimately depends on divine grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If even the scholars who inquire only rarely reach truth without divine grace, how much do you rely on your own intellect? Have you sincerely asked Allah for tawfiq to know Him truly, or do you assume your current understanding is sufficient?
